Japanese Police Arrest Koreans in Sinuiju 70

Korean Workers Angrily Go on Strike

Andong Correspondence: According to people from Pyongyang, Korean workers in the area went on strike out of anger due to the large-scale arrest of Koreans by the Japanese police. This has been reported in various newspapers. Unexpectedly, a similar incident occurred in Sinuiju today (the 4th), which is very noteworthy. The reporter briefly records the situation as follows:

When the Sinuiju Incident occurred in Korea, the Japanese police arrested three Koreans due to the protest of our Consul Zhu Fu, in order to cover up our people's ears and eyes. Now that the riots have subsided for many days, the Japanese police suddenly launched a surprise large-scale arrest of Koreans. At the same time, they are trying their best to publicize how hard the Japanese police have worked for the riot. As of the beginning of this month, more and more Koreans have been arrested. Whether they were personally involved in the riot or not, anyone who slightly violates their intentions is on the list of arrests. As a result, the Koreans were offended, leading to a strike event unprecedented since the Japanese rule of Korea.

Initially, the Pingan North Provincial Government in Sinuiju wanted to carry out construction projects, called "Pingan North Province Poor People Relief Civil Engineering Projects". The main purpose of this project is to build Sinuiju City into a major city on the border with our country. The secondary purpose is to build roads in Pingan North Province. Most of the workers are Koreans, with a part of overseas Chinese, and led by the Japanese. It has been under construction since last year and has not been interrupted so far. It is a group work. The strikers this time are the workers of the Maeda Group, a total of 220 people. Since the 13th of last month, they have been building trunk roads in Uminemachi, Sinuiju. The Japanese police have been arresting Koreans on a daily basis. One person in the Maeda Group was also arrested. His colleagues were very angry and went on strike simultaneously at 10 a.m. on the 4th.

After the strike, the Japanese police reported one instigator, fearing that arresting everyone would encourage the trend, and to prevent other workers from striking, they tried their best to suppress it. On the one hand, they tried to cover up the reasons for the strike, because Koreans' anti-Chinese sentiment was to cater to the Japanese, but they were arrested after the event. Therefore, the Koreans were very angry. They used to be accomplices of the tiger, but now they are bitten by the tiger, which is what they deserve. The Japanese did not want to announce the truth about the strike, so they covered up their words, saying that the workers went on strike because of wage issues. In the past, the daily wage for each person was 40 cents, but recently it was reduced to 35 cents. The driver of the truck used to get 3 cents per trip, but recently it was reduced to 2.5 cents. Because of this, the Koreans were dissatisfied, leading to the strike. However, if it was only because of wage issues, there have been many similar events in the past, why have no strikes been seen, but only today? The reason is difficult to understand. Sinuiju has been very uneasy since this incident. The streets are full of Japanese police to suppress it. But it is not known where the Japanese police were when the Korean incident occurred in the past. (August 4)

Suppressing Bandits

Blocking and Suppressing the Red Bandits Fleeing to Western Jiangxi 71

Red Bandits Flee to the Border of Hunan and Jiangxi in Three Routes

Chen and He are Assigned to Block and Pursue

Hunan Army Will Also Launch a Pincer Attack in Western Jiangxi

Nanchang Correspondence: The Red Bandits in Jiangxi originally numbered about 100,000 people with about 100,000 guns. Its main forces, such as the pseudo-Third Army Peng Dehuai, the Fourth Army Huang Gonglue, and the Fifth Army Lin Biao, were resolved by the suppression bandit army in the battles of Tangtang, Wenhua, Luokou, Longgang, Donggu, etc. More than half of the bandits were eliminated. The remnants gathered in Yudu, Xingguo, Huichang, Ruijin, and Jianghang in western Fujian, with about tens of thousands of people and guns. Now the suppression bandit army is advancing step by step to the bandit areas of Xing, Yu, Rui, and Hui. Therefore, the bandits fled to western Jiangxi again. Even the troops of Xiang Ying and Luo Binghui in western Fujian retreated to Huichang and Ruijin, and then retreated from Hui and Rui to the area between Yudu and Xingguo, and retreated to the border of Jiangxi and Hunan in separate routes. Recently, the General Headquarters reported based on aircraft reports that there were no large-scale armed bandits in Ruijin and Huichang, and the recapture was not a problem. Even Yudu and Xingguo only had a few armed bandits covering the westward escape of most of the Red Bandits. It is said that the escape plan of the Red Bandits is divided into three routes. The main forces of Zhu, Mao, Peng, and Huang will, one, escape from Yudu along the Gongshui River through the north of Ganxian to Chongyi and Shangyou; one, cross Wan'an from Xingguo and Yudu to Suichuan; and one, pass through Taihe and advance to Ninggang from Xingguo. Their common goal is to occupy the old lair of Jinggang or harass eastern Hunan. The vanguard of Zhu and Mao's troops has reached the east bank of the Ganjiang River, preparing to cross the river westward. The atmosphere in Taihe, Wan'an, and Ganxian is extremely tense. Commander-in-Chief Jiang immediately ordered Chen Mingshu's troops to block the Ganjiang River, while He Yingqin's troops were solely responsible for the pursuit, and ordered the Hunan Army to exit eastern Hunan to western Jiangxi and launch a pincer attack on the bandits. It is said that the Hunan Army had long been prepared for the bandits in western Jiangxi. Now that they have received news of Zhu and Mao's westward escape, they have added powerful troops and Chen has stationed troops on the border of Gan, preparing to block them. If necessary, they will cross the border into western Jiangxi to eliminate the Red Bandits. (August 4)

Hunan Merchants and People Oppose the Production Tax 72

Submit a Petition to the Provincial Government Stating Six Reasons for Repealing It

Changsha Correspondence: After Hunan Province implemented the abolition of the consolidated tax, it suddenly lost 600,000 to 700,000 yuan of income per month. Although the central government subsidized 200,000 yuan per month, the monthly revenue from the business tax was only more than 70,000 yuan, so the difference was still large and could not be made up. Government expenses were in arrears for more than five months, and the current situation was difficult to maintain. Zhang Kailian, the director of the Finance Department, therefore submitted a proposal to the provincial government for approval to start a production tax on special items, specifying a total of ten categories of coal, oil, bamboo, wood, paper, etc. produced in Hunan Province, and collecting a production tax of 2% to 5% of the value. It was started on June 20, and it was expected to generate more than 200,000 yuan per month to help subsidize the expenses. However, the United Association of Chambers of Commerce of Hunan Province strongly opposed this as a new tax similar to likin. Yesterday, it especially listed six major reasons and petitioned the provincial government to abolish it immediately. At the same time, four representatives were elected to go to the central government in Beijing to file a petition. The spring petition to the provincial government to abolish the tax stated, "The case investigates the proposal of the representatives of the counties at the Second Congress of the Association. The main text states that the Hunan Finance Department's creation of a production tax on special items is similar to likin and should be repealed. The reason is that the National Government has clearly ordered the abolition of likin and strictly prohibits the establishment of any tax similar to likin. The orders are so strict that they should be jointly observed. Hunan was the first to abolish the consolidated tax and implement the business tax. Your Excellency's love for merchants and people is also extremely exhaustive. Unexpectedly, the order to abolish likin has just been issued, and the order to collect a tax similar to likin has been issued again. The business tax has just been launched, and the production tax is about to be collected again. Although the competent financial officer has a suffering that he cannot but endure, it seems a pity to set up such a name and put the provincial government in a position of defying the central government. In order to respect the law, it should be repealed. 1. Since Zhang Jingyao's scourge of Hunan, followed by the plundering of the Shield Regiment, it has been almost completely exploited. Fortunately, the revolutionary army rose up and Your Excellency presided over the Hunan government. The people celebrated the arrival of the Soviets and were comforted by the hope of clouds and rain. Unexpectedly, Zhang Gui caused trouble in the past, and the Red Bandits destroyed it in the future. The vitality was depleted, and the people were dying nine times out of ten. The reason why they can barely survive is by selling this small number of products in the market to make a living. If the government destroys it again, then the vitality will be cut off. In order to maintain people's livelihood, it should be repealed. 2. Water and drought disasters occur every year. In addition, the bandits and communists run rampant, the fields are deserted, and the forests are lost, I don't know how many. The tax rates for products are all necessary for daily use, such as coal and oil. Even beggars need to use them. Those who operate in this business are only seeking small profits. As for paper, most of it comes from Pingliu, a place spared from the tiger's mouth, and it is again attacked. It seems difficult to feel at ease in terms of sentiment. In order to relieve the disaster victims, it should be repealed. 3. Hunan's business tax has not yet developed and is being persuaded in many ways. Now a new tax is being revived. The people will inevitably become more suspicious. Although various products are transported out of Hunan Province, both business tax and production tax are levied. Who will believe that it is not a double tax? Moreover, avoiding cards is restored again, and there are difficulties everywhere. Even if the government is honest, it is inevitable that there are places where it cannot see or hear. In order to avoid double taxation, it should be repealed. 4. The national tax must be levied on a certain thing that is considered to have considerable benefits or must be gradually prohibited. For example, the income tax is levied because it has net profit income. The business tax has considerable benefits. The special tax on tobacco and alcohol is levied on consumption and poison. The government's prohibition in levy is sincere and profound. If the products are all necessary for people's lives, it is not yet known whether the operators can profit from them. However, local products and exports are subject to extra tax, which is equivalent to importing foreign goods and causing the outflow of profit rights. Hunan's finances are depleted and cannot sell products to absorb cash inflows to seek relief. How can the economy of officials and people develop? In order to regulate finance, it should be repealed. 5. The southwest of Hunan is mostly mountainous, and the harvest is always small. If the government considers the income from mountainous areas to be equal to the income from fields, it feels very unfair. All countries in the world that levy land tax, except for fields and houses, have not heard of taking from mountains and forests. Our National Government has repeatedly ordered afforestation to harmonize the climate and to open up and cultivate. If the government taxes barren mountains, it means that those who abandon mountains can easily bear the burden, while those who cultivate mountains find it troublesome. In order to encourage afforestation, it should be repealed. 6. Measures: (1) Petition the government to abolish the production tax on special items and implement the business tax to reduce the suffering of merchants and people. (2) Ask the government to submit another petition to the central government, considering that Hunan Province is a special disaster area and respects the central government's laws and regulations, it should be subsidized monthly in a preferential manner to make up for the abolition of likin," etc. The conference resolved and unanimously approved the proposal and recorded it in the file. It should be prepared to submit a document to your government for review and approval to order the Finance Department to abolish it as soon as possible to sympathize with the difficulties of merchants and relieve the people's difficulties. There is no end to the wait for orders."

Liaoning Relief Financial Measures 74

Issuing Circulating Bonds of Five Million Yuan

Shenyang Correspondence: Liaoning Province has been affected by the world's expensive gold and cheap silver, and the export of agricultural products has been stagnant. In addition, the Feng banknotes are scarce and the finances are extremely tight. The Liaoning Provincial Government, in view of this, believes that in order to maintain public security, it must start with relieving finances. It has ordered the Departments of Civil Affairs, Finance, and Industry to jointly formulate relief measures. They have been submitted to the 231st Provincial Committee meeting on the 28th of last month for discussion. The meeting immediately passed the measures, which contain a total of thirteen articles. The main points are as follows: (1) Issuing circulating bonds of five million yuan; (2) The purpose of the bonds is purely to relieve the finances of the counties and maintain the local market. The circulation period is set at one year; (3) The types of bonds are divided into four types: ten yuan, five yuan, one yuan, and five jiao; (4) When the bonds are issued, those distributed to a certain county will have a small county name stamp added to the surface of the ticket to indicate the difference and avoid unscrupulous merchants buying and transferring them; (5) The bonds are valued at the same price as the current foreign currency in the county where they are circulated and may not be discounted; (6) In addition to circulating in the market, the bonds are also allowed to be used to pay mu donations, land taxes, and miscellaneous taxes; (7) After one year from the date of issuance, all bonds will be collected by the counties and submitted to the province for destruction to avoid abuses. According to Liaoning Province, it issued 20 million yuan of agricultural and commercial loans in the spring of this year. Because the conditions were too harsh, there were very few applicants. This time, the measures have been improved, and the principle of benefiting the people has been established, so that there will be no difficulties and all will share the benefits, and the people will be widely benefited. (August 2)

English Female Aviator

Aimee Johnson Arrives in Shenyang 76

Immediately Flies to Japan

Shenyang Correspondence: British female aviator Aimee Johnson, who is flying between London and Tokyo, arrived in Shenyang at 1:45 PM on the 5th, accompanied by technician Han Humphreys, piloting the Jason II aircraft. They landed at Dongta Airfield. A large crowd of Chinese and foreigners gathered to offer a warm welcome. The Aviation Headquarters presented a bouquet of fresh flowers, and the British Consul-General, Mr. Isitt, offered a bottle of champagne in celebration. Ms. Johnson and her companion briefly rested in the hall of the Aviation Headquarters. After the aircraft was refueled by the Asiatic Petroleum Company at the airfield, it took off at 2:40 PM, flying along the railway line past the border at Andong towards Gyeongseong, Korea, with an estimated arrival time of 8:00 PM. After refueling, they will fly directly to Tokyo. The enthusiastic atmosphere at the airfield at the time is recorded as follows: Ms. Johnson's original itinerary planned for her to arrive in Shenyang on the 3rd. However, due to weather conditions in Russia, her schedule was delayed. After arriving in Chita on the 3rd, she sent a telegram to the British Consulate-General in Shenyang at 5:00 PM, simply stating that she would arrive in Shenyang on the 5th to refuel. Upon receiving the telegram, the British Consulate anticipated her arrival in Shenyang around the morning of the 5th and informed British merchants in Shenyang and relevant Chinese and foreign parties. At 9:30 AM on the 5th, Feng Yong arrived at the airfield in his own Bili aircraft, and twenty students, led by teachers, also arrived by car to welcome her. The British Consul-General, Yu Zuolian, the European and American secretary of the Diplomatic Commissioner's Office, and Mr. She Naoman, the Shenyang Customs Commissioner, arrived at 10:00 AM. By 10:30 AM, British merchants, both men and women, had arrived in cars and gathered at the airfield. Zhou Dehong, an attache of the Aviation Headquarters, along with members and technicians, greeted the guests. At 11:00 AM, the airfield received news that Ms. Johnson had departed from Hailar Airfield at 4:30 AM that morning. At 12:00 PM, further news arrived that she had landed in Harbin at 10:30 AM and taken off at 11:00 AM, passing over Changchun at 11:50 AM. After 12:00 PM, Feng Yong flew his Bili aircraft 300 li north of Shenyang for the first time to welcome her, but did not see her aircraft. He returned and reported that the weather to the north was poor. Twenty minutes later, he flew out a second time. Bo Lei, a technician from the Aviation Headquarters, also flew north in another aircraft to investigate, but still did not see her aircraft. The wind was blowing from the north that day, slightly hindering the flight. At 1:30 PM, the sound of an engine was finally heard, and Aimee's aircraft was spotted. Feng Yong and Bo Lei each flew their aircraft to meet her, circling once. At 1:40 PM, the welcoming aircraft landed first, followed by Aimee's aircraft. A crowd of Chinese and foreign men and women gathered around Aimee's aircraft. The British Consul-General was the first to approach the aircraft, shake Aimee's hand, and offer congratulations and welcome, shouting "Hooray" three times. The entire crowd followed suit, then shook hands with Ms. Johnson and exchanged greetings. For a time, the crowd eager to see Ms. Johnson was extremely congested. The British Consul-General presented a bottle of champagne and a letter of introduction, which included letters of introduction and telegrams for her trip to Japan, as well as a permit from the Japanese government to enter the country. Then,

Page 12

Zhou, the attache of the Aviation Headquarters, delivered a welcoming speech and presented a bouquet of fresh flowers as a memento. Subsequently, he led Ms. Johnson, the technician, the British Consul-General, and other well-wishers to rest inside the headquarters, where they were served champagne and pastries. Ms. Johnson was wearing a yellow linen flying suit and was poised and generous. She is 28 years old and unmarried. During the break, she discussed her previous flights with the British expatriates. The aircraft Ms. Johnson is flying was manufactured in 1930 by Blackburn Aircraft. It is specially marked as Jason II, with a speed of 110 miles per hour, equivalent to 450 li in Chinese measurement, a maximum speed of 140 miles, a load capacity of 2,050 pounds, a horsepower of 105, and seating for two people. The purpose of the trip is for sightseeing.

Ms. Johnson previously flew Jason I on a flight to Australia. This trip began at 1:23 AM on the 28th from Lympne Airfield in London, passing through Berlin and arriving in Moscow at 10:30 PM that evening. She departed the next day, landing in Smolensk to refuel before continuing her flight. On the morning of the 31st, she flew to Omsk, taking off at 8:20 AM and arriving in Krasnoyarsk in the evening. She then flew to Irkutsk, followed by Chita. On the 5th, at 5:15 AM, she entered Chinese territory at Hailar, landing in Harbin at 10:30 AM. Diplomatic officials, British consular staff, and expatriate merchants gave her a grand welcome. She took off at 11:00 AM, passing over Changchun at 11:50 AM, and landed in Shenyang at 1:45 PM. After refueling, Ms. Johnson bid farewell and took off in her aircraft at 2:40 PM, heading for Gyeongseong, Korea. According to Ms. Johnson, she will fly back to London along the original route in about two weeks. Han Humphreys, the technician accompanying Ms. Johnson on the flight, is 27 years old and a renowned engineer from the London Aeronautical Society. (August 6th)

Suppression of Bandits Amidst the Flood in Northern Anhui 77

Suppression Troops Battle Bandits in the Water in Three Counties

Bandit Leader Killed, Several Hostages Rescued

Bengbu Correspondence: In recent years, disasters have frequently occurred in northern Anhui, and the people's livelihood has been impoverished. During the summer of this year, floods caused widespread devastation, and the disaster situation in the counties along the Huai River was particularly severe. The scale of the floods across the country is probably unsurpassed here. Amidst the vast flood, Fengtai County has also suffered from bandit disturbances, with murder and arson rampant. With natural disasters not yet over, man-made disasters have struck again. Alas, the common people have nowhere to die. Fengtai is located in the Huai River basin. The continuous heavy rains and flash floods have turned the entire county into a watery expanse, with fields, homes, and crops all submerged. The dead have been swept away, and the living have been displaced. It is already heartbreaking and distressing. However, in the areas of Dianzi Market, Gugou Market, Taiping Market, Tianjia Market, and Gongjia Market, bandit leaders Liu Chuanjin, Xu Guanming, Yang Xinshan, and Deng Dagizi led over 500 fierce bandits to occupy and harass the area. They intercepted merchant ships on the Changhuai River, looted the food of the villagers, and after looting, they arbitrarily burned, killed, and seized over 200 firearms from the local people's self-defense corps. They killed a gentleman named Chen and the entire family of a Mr. Su, and there were many other victims. Traffic on the Changhuai River was disrupted. The bandits even threatened to attack Fengtai Zhengyang and other places, planning a large-scale riot. Upon hearing this, Ni Rongxian, the commander of the bandit suppression forces in Shou, Feng, and Huai counties, immediately led his troops on the 3rd of this month, together with the police teams of the Huaiyuan Changhuai Water Public Security Bureau and the independent battalion of the Provisional Second Brigade stationed in Shou, aboard the Fu Bo, Bao Tai, and Ji Hang vessels, rushing to Dianzi Market, Gugou Market, Qijia Market, and other places to assist in the suppression. They surrounded and fiercely attacked the bandits led by Liu Chuanjin and Deng Dagizi, killing several bandit leaders such as Liu Chuanjin on the spot, capturing seven bandits and suspects alive, rescuing nine male and female hostages, and seizing one Mauser pistol, three rifles, and several stones of stolen wheat. At that time, the bandits could not withstand the assault and fled westward. The next morning (the 4th), the government troops continued to pursue. The bandits fled towards Ping'a Mountain. All units advanced by land and water, pursuing them to Taojia Weizi, across the river from Taiping Market. The bandits, aboard dozens of civilian boats, opened fire to resist when they saw the government troops approaching. The government troops besieged them from the steamers. Just as they were engaged in a fierce battle, a torrential downpour began, accompanied by strong winds. The bandits took the opportunity to scatter and flee. The soldiers bravely swam after them, but the current was too swift, and they nearly drowned. They killed two bandits, Cao Chuanshun and Li Wenxue, captured six bandits and suspects alive, and rescued eight hostages. The remaining bandits all escaped. The officers and soldiers of the Shou, Feng, and Huai counties bandit suppression command returned to the Shun Geng Mountain headquarters in Huaiyuan on the 5th to rest. They will wait for the bandits' whereabouts to be ascertained before continuing the pursuit. (August 6th)

Recent Situation in Guizhou 78

Guizhou Correspondence: Guizhou, as a province remotely located in the southwest, has very little opportunity to interact with people from other provinces. Furthermore, it lacks substantial industries that could be recognized by the people of the country. Therefore, today, whenever the name "Guizhou" is mentioned, it is necessary to associate it with the neighboring province of Yunnan and say "Yunnan and Guizhou" in order to evoke an image in the listener's mind, as if there is indeed a Guizhou province located near Yunnan province. This is not due to the country's lack of attention, but rather due to the people of Guizhou's lack of competitiveness, their inability to make a significant impression on the people of the country through their achievements and thus attract their attention. However, since Guizhou is a province of the Republic of China and not outside its territory, everything in its society and politics is closely related to the entire Republic of China. It certainly does not become an exception simply because it is located in a remote corner and is not noticed by the people of the country. Therefore, the current social and political situation in Guizhou is indeed necessary to introduce to the people of the country, which will also be welcomed by readers who are concerned about the southwest region.

Since everything in Guizhou has long been isolated from the people of the country, it is necessary to briefly trace its past and report on its general situation before successively introducing its present. This will allow those who care about Guizhou to understand why the present situation exists, and it will facilitate discussion or promote its progress. The following is a detailed description:

1. People's Characteristics and General Living Conditions: Guizhou is full of mountains, and its resources are abundant but underdeveloped. The majority of the people rely on handicrafts and farming for self-sufficiency. If they slack off in their work, they will face the threat of freezing and starvation. Therefore, they have developed a spirit of endurance and hard work, unafraid of hardship and danger. Unfortunately, due to inconvenient transportation, they are limited in their knowledge and cannot broaden their narrow minds. Therefore, it is easy to govern them but difficult to lead them. They are able to endure the oppression of warlords and bureaucrats, as well as the exploitation of local tyrants and evil gentry, without showing any resistance. The prevalence of corrupt officials in Guizhou today is due to this.

2. Politics: Guizhou society is a feudal society, so Guizhou politics is also feudal politics. Although there have been many changes since the founding of the Republic, political life has always been entrusted to military force. It is only seen as a tool of military force, giving the people the deepest suffering. Politics is cut off from the people, which further weakens the foundation of military force, leading to an unstable state. The people also have no time to rest and recuperate. Therefore, the political history of Guizhou over the past 20 years has been marked by the dominance of military force and the extraction of resources from the people by military force, with no trace of true political meaning. What politics is there to speak of?

3. Military Affairs: In the early years of the Republic of China, the number of troops in Guizhou was extremely small. Since the wars of Protecting the Constitution and Protecting the Nation, Guizhou Province followed the initial uprising, and the number of troops gradually increased, expanding from one division to five brigades. By the 13th and 14th years of the Republic, it had expanded further to seven divisions. They mostly took from their neighbors and provided supplies to other provinces. Therefore, although Guizhou was considered poor, it did not deeply feel the pain of having too many troops. The military power was unified, and there were few phenomena of division and mutual suspicion and prevention. In the 15th year of the Republic, Yuan Zuming led all his troops out of Hunan to participate in the revolution, leaving only one division under Zhou Xicheng to garrison Guizhou. After Yuan's death, the troops outside the province became the 9th, 10th, and 43rd Armies, each working independently and not connected. Zhou Xicheng's troops inside the province also suddenly expanded from one division and were reorganized into the 25th Army. Since then, the Guizhou military system has been completely broken. The troops outside the province were fortunate to be able to rely on the Guizhou people's spirit of endurance and hard work, unafraid of hardship and danger, and worked hard to fight. Although few of them remain today, their merits are firmly recorded in the party and the country. Currently, only a part of the 25th Army in the province is led by Mao Guangxiang, who is in charge of Guizhou. Among those stationed outside the province are Jia Lie's unit (a part of the 25th Army), which is suppressing bandits in the Xiang-Qian border area, Xie Bin's newly formed 10th Division, Li Bohua's Independent 2nd Brigade, Wang Guangzhong's newly formed Independent 18th Brigade, and Luo Qijiang's newly formed Independent 19th Brigade, which are suppressing the Communists in the Hubei area. All the Guizhou troops are here.

4. Education: Since Guizhou is located in a remote corner and transportation is inconvenient, the education system is naturally behind that of other provinces. Moreover, the education funds are too small to support consolidation. The number of primary and secondary schools that have taken a basic form is extremely limited. Fortunately, many private schools have been established by local sages and pioneers, who have donated funds, and their results are also superior. The provincial schools have been declining due to the instability of the political situation or the failure to provide education funds on time or in the correct amount. The education center is purely built on private groups, which is also a unique phenomenon in Guizhou.

5. Finance and Government: Guizhou is one of the poorest provinces in China. Before the 6th year of the Republic, the annual income was only three to four million yuan. After the 7th year of the Republic, military affairs gradually expanded, and the military expenses required increased day by day. The government worked hard to increase revenue, and the income increased sharply, with annual tax revenue reaching six to seven million yuan. Since then, financiers have increased tax revenue to ingratiate themselves with the military authorities and to solidify their power and position as their sole purpose, exhausting their abilities. To this day, the annual income has reached seventeen to eighteen million yuan. The productivity of the people today is not stronger than that of the 6th and 7th years of the Republic, but they are burdened with more than five times the amount, so the people's finances are exhausted and it is difficult to sustain them for long. The government's expenditures have never had a budget. Although there is a huge annual income, it is only said that military and political expenses are sometimes insufficient, and the people are relentlessly exploited. The darkness of Guizhou's finances is unique among the provinces.

Songjiang 81

People from the Four Counties Request Punishment of Bandits: Li Wenjun, the pseudo-chief of staff of Tai Bao A Shu's troops, Zhao Guomin, the pseudo-regimental commander, and He Yinyu and Dai Kechang, the pseudo-battalion commanders, were arrested one after another. They were escorted to the province by provincial order to be interrogated and dealt with by the Security Office. It has been more than a month since then, and there has been no news of their punishment. The Security and Preservation Committee of the four counties of Jin, Song, Jia, and Ping stated that the banditry has been rampant for years, and the number of victims in the four counties is no less than thousands of families. Since the joint suppression by the four counties, the full force of the army and police on land and water has been used, and huge rewards have been offered to capture the ferocious bandits and thieves one by one. The four bandits, Li, Zhao, He, and Dai, have committed numerous crimes, and the evidence is conclusive. Since they were sent to the province, there has been no news. A telegram was sent to Commander Cao, requesting that he forward it to his superiors, requesting that the bandits be publicly executed as soon as possible to appease public opinion. Commander Cao has approved the request and telegraphed it to the Provincial Security Office, requesting that it be forwarded to the Provincial Government for the early execution of the bandits. According to the people of Zhuangjia Hangzhen, Fengxian County, the entire town was burned and killed by the Communist bandits throughout the year, and the bandit leader Li Wenjun belonged to this case. The people of Zhuanghang all have a deep hatred. Kunshan 82

Fire Brigade Member Insulted for No Reason: Since the opening of the Kunshan Public Theater, the manager, Ma Jikang, has repeatedly caused trouble. The Public Security Bureau went to investigate several times, but found nothing and let it go, causing Ma to become even more unscrupulous. At 11:00 PM on the 7th, a Wang family on Xingxue Road suddenly reported carelessness. Zhu Changsheng, a member of the Central Three District Fire Brigade, happened to be taking a nap in front of the theater. Upon hearing the alarm, he blew his police whistle to gather his colleagues and rushed to the rescue. Unexpectedly, he angered Ma, who dragged Zhu into the theater and ordered the patrol officers on the scene to take him to the bureau for handling. Fortunately, the patrol officers were unmoved, and hundreds of spectators persuaded Zhu to leave, believing that Ma was too unreasonable. After the members of the district rescued the fire and returned to the district, they learned of the situation and were greatly dissatisfied. They convened an emergency meeting of all members at 3:00 PM this afternoon (the 8th) and reported the situation to the Joint Association, requesting negotiations with Ma. If there is no satisfactory reply, all members will resign from their duties.

Suzhou 83

Request to Use Road Construction Funds to Build Dike: The Suzhou County Chamber of Commerce, in view of the severe flooding in the county this summer, which was unseen in 40 years, and witnessing the tragic situation, deeply understands the great relationship between agriculture and commerce. Moreover, most of the land in Suzhou County is rice paddies, which rely on the benefits of the lake water. There are field banks but no dikes, so the entire lake overflows without a way to drain. It takes time for the water to recede, so what remedy can be said? Suzhou County's tax quota is the highest in the country, and the construction fees collected annually are also the highest in the province, but agricultural water conservancy has never been considered. At this critical juncture, there is an urgent need to provide relief. Therefore, it submitted a report to the Provincial Government Construction Department yesterday (the 8th), requesting that the construction of county roads in the county be suspended for one year, and that the road construction funds be used to build low-lying field dikes to provide work relief. It requested that Suzhou County be considered as a financial region, where national expenses are derived, and that a special change be made to protect the disaster victims and ensure agriculture.

Local People Request Changes to Street Widths: More than 20 local people, including Pan Shengnian, Ding Yuqing, and Zhang Zhongren, jointly submitted a report to the Suzhou Provincial Government, the Construction Department, and the Suzhou County Government yesterday (the 8th), stating that the street width in Suzhou City was previously resolved by the Administrative Committee during the era of the Municipal Preparatory Office to be 10 meters as the standard. Later, the Municipal Government repeatedly changed it to 14 meters. Since its implementation, the business districts of Guanqian Street, Jingde Road, and other places have gradually declined. It should be requested that the width of streets that have not yet been widened be based on the previously determined standard for implementation. The files of the former Municipal Preparatory Office should be quickly retrieved, and the county should be ordered to convene a meeting of local people to determine that the widest street should be 10 meters as the standard, and the Construction Bureau should be ordered to comply.

The High Court Transfers Trial Judges: Mo Zongyou, a judge of the Jiangsu High Court, has been ordered to be promoted to prosecutor of the Supreme Court. The vacancy will be filled by Fang Wen, the presiding judge of the Jiangning District Court. In addition, Ji Kuancheng, a trial judge of Gaoyou County, has requested leave, and Jiang Youhua has been appointed to act as his agent.

Changshu 84

County Magistrate Seals Off Thunder God Temple: It is a local custom here to celebrate the birthday of the Thunder God on the 23rd day of the sixth month of the lunar calendar every year. The incense is very prosperous, and the city gates in various places are open all night. Vendors are concentrated in Shimei, and their profits are tripled. However, since last year, the county party headquarters resolved to prohibit the opening, so the incense has decreased slightly. Now, the Thunder God's birthday is approaching again, and the party headquarters has again resolved to request the county government to strictly prohibit it. After the county government approved the letter, it ordered the Public Security Bureau to quickly implement it. On the morning of the 6th, Director Yin ordered Officer Cheng of the first branch station to go to Shimei to seal off the Thunder God Temple.

The Notorious Bandit Zheng Ming Was Arrested Again in Shanghai: After the bandit leader Zheng Yushan was arrested in Shanghai by the county government of this county and was found guilty after interrogation and executed by shooting, his son Zheng Ming (who served as a commander in the bandit gang and roamed the northeastern countryside, robbing the Western Yangzhen, etc.) planned to take revenge. Recently, he has been harassing the coastal areas of Wangshi, Fushan, and Bai Mao Kou, claiming to avenge his father, so the coastal residents have been unable to sleep peacefully. Unexpectedly, the Public Security Bureau of this county received a message from Shanghai on the 5th that the notorious bandit Zheng Ming was arrested in Zhabei, Shanghai, by Detective Xu, together with the local security corps, and a Browning pistol was found. He has now been sent to the Xinzha police station for detention. A telegram was immediately sent to Changshu to send police to escort him back. Currently, the Public Security Bureau here sent a team of eight cannon squad members and four detectives to Shanghai on the 6th to escort him back.

After the Power Plant Stopped Supplying Electricity: This power plant was originally scheduled to stop supplying electricity for two weeks from July 9th to replace new machinery. However, almost a month has passed, and it has not been able to restore power. Users have been in darkness every day, and businesses have been greatly affected invisibly. The power plant has not yet made any formal announcement. Therefore, 52 shops in the southern district have jointly requested the users association to convene a meeting to discuss dealing with the plant and urge it to release electricity as soon as possible.

Wuxi 85

Regulations for Each County to Collect Land Survey Fees: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs and Department of Finance, regarding the collection of land survey fees in various counties of Jiangsu Province, had previously instructed the Provincial Land Bureau to investigate the situation in each county and revise the plan for phased collection. Subsequently, the bureau responded with suggestions that counties that had completed land surveys should have their collection quotas appropriately reduced and the collection period shortened; counties that had not completed the surveys should have the collection period shortened; and those that had collected fees but not completed the surveys should follow a two-tiered approach: (A) If the collected fees had been completely used, collection should begin in accordance with the general plan, starting from the year of commencement; (B) If the collected fees had been used but a balance remained, the collection quota should be reduced in the final year depending on the amount of the balance. Subsequently, the Department of Civil Affairs and Department of Finance reviewed the circumstances of each county and formulated collection methods accordingly: (1) Kunshan and Baoshan counties, which had completed land surveys, would have their collection reduced by half to five cents per mu, temporarily for one year; (2) Nantong and Rugao counties, which had not completed land surveys, would collect ten cents per mu, temporarily for one year; (3) Chongming and Jiading counties, which had already collected land survey fees, would collect ten cents per mu, temporarily for two years; (4) Nantong and Qidong counties, which needed to commence work early, should begin collecting one year ahead of schedule, starting in the 20th year of the Republic; (5) Shanghai County: due to Article 1, Paragraphs 1 and 2 of the resolution of the provincial and municipal division of administrative power conference regarding land survey, there are already clear regulations. The county is currently requesting a return of funds and has separately requested the Shanghai Municipal Government to consult and handle the matter, with the method to be determined after consultation. The remaining counties will begin collection according to their respective commencement years. After the Land Bureau is established, the situation will be further investigated and handled appropriately.

The Department of Civil Affairs Rectifies Grain Reserves in Each County: In the 18th year of the Republic, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs ordered each county to purchase and store grain with all accumulated funds for grain reserves, without any excuses. However, the storage warehouses in each county were mostly dilapidated, and some funds had been diverted to other uses, making it difficult to find alternative locations. Therefore, although many counties complied with the order to purchase and store grain, they delayed implementation. Diversion and embezzlement were also not uncommon. This year, continuous rain caused disasters, and a good autumn harvest is unlikely. Rectifying grain reserves and providing disaster relief are now extremely urgent. Director Hu has specially drafted nine standard measures for replenishing warehouses in each county and recovering embezzled funds, and has appointed Jiang Fuqin to Wuxian, Changshu, Kunshan, Wuxi, Wujin, and Jiangyin; Wu Xie to Songjiang, Nanhui, Qingpu, Fengxian, Jinshan, and Taicang; Yu Shoufan to Jiading, Chongming, Haimen, Jurong, and Danyang; and Shi Zhizhi to Nantong, Rugao, Xinghua, Taixian, and Gaoyou to supervise the county magistrates in their earnest implementation. The remaining 39 counties, including Zhenjiang and Jiangdu, are strictly ordered to be responsible for the implementation.

The Section Affairs Dispute in the 17th District Remains Unresolved: The entire township head of the 17th district of the county, Zheng Shaohong, and 37 others, disagreed with the section chief Hua Sigǔ. They jointly submitted their resignations to the county government. County Magistrate Chen summoned section chief Hua Sigǔ and township head Zheng Shaohong to the county on the 27th of last month for a personal inquiry. Since the issues raised were all minor, he ordered them to prioritize the local area, work together harmoniously, be open and honest, and seek happiness for the people. The previous issues were not to be discussed. The township heads all agreed and withdrew. After returning to their townships, they felt that the county government's handling was not thorough. Yesterday, they held an emergency meeting, chaired by Xi Wenxuan, and resolved that until section chief Hua Sigǔ was removed, section affairs would be temporarily maintained by the joint office of township heads.

Daughters-in-Law Disagree, One Hangs Herself: Pu A Jin, a villager from Lane 381, Lao Pu Lane, 11th District (South Yanshi), was 24 years old and married to Cai, who was 20 years old. Pu had four brothers, all working as assistants in Shanghai's Changsan brothels. After A Jin married in the 18th year of the Republic, the couple's relationship was initially harmonious. However, due to the stirring up of trouble by his sisters-in-law, the relationship gradually deteriorated, leading to discord between the daughters-in-law and frequent arguments. A Jin repeatedly beat Cai. Cai told her mother's family, who were unable to intervene, and could only sigh in despair. Cai, filled with resentment, developed a desire to end her life. On the morning of the 7th, at around 7:00 AM, she changed into new clothes and shoes in her room, took a hemp rope, hung it from the beam, and hanged herself. It is said that Cai was seven months pregnant, resulting in two deaths. Neighbors lamented the tragedy.

A Vicious Stepmother Causes Her Stepchild to Drown: Lu, the manager of Liu Fuji's trough workshop outside the South Gate of the county, at Jie Jing Bridge on the South Shangtang, was over 40 years old and had a son and a daughter. His son, Xiang Jin, was currently 10 years old. His wife had passed away. Lu, unaccustomed to sleeping alone, was introduced by a colleague to a woman surnamed Li from Qishuyan to be his second wife. After she entered the family, the couple's love was extremely strong, but they did not have any children. Instead, she often abused his son. The day before, she forced Xiang Jin to wash his pants at Qing Ting Bang. He accidentally fell into the river and drowned. Afterwards, Lu returned home from the shop and learned of the incident. He rushed to retrieve the body. It took about an hour to recover Xiang Jin's body. It was a tragic scene.

A Kidnapping Gang is Broken Up: In the Huashan area south of the county and the Qishan area east of the county, kidnapping cases have occurred frequently recently. The judgment has been made, and its main text is as follows: The original judgment is revoked. Jiang Hong, intending to unlawfully enrich himself, used deception to cause another person to deliver his own property. He is sentenced to a fine of 200 yuan, which can be converted to one day of imprisonment for each yuan if not paid. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be offset against the fine at the rate of one yuan per day. Jiang Hong shall return 1,000 yuan in silver dollars to Ji Shashi, as well as a 3,000-yuan village bank passbook from Gongji, and ten 100-yuan village bank notes issued by Chengfeng Village.

Zhenjiang 89

Submitting Reports on the Survey of Disaster Areas: The Zhenjiang County Government sent members to various districts the day before yesterday to conduct a survey of the flood situation together with the district heads and members of the Finance Bureau in order to compile a report to the Department of Civil Affairs. The members have submitted a detailed report on the disaster situation in each district to the county government, which has been forwarded to the Department of Civil Affairs to request disaster relief. The situation in each disaster area is briefly recorded as follows: (District 1) More than 23,300 mu of farmland were flooded, more than 40 houses collapsed, and the number of disaster victims is approximately 12,100. (District 2) A total of more than 20,700 mu of farmland were flooded, with approximately 9,700 disaster victims. (District 3) More than 15,900 mu of farmland were flooded, with approximately 11,900 disaster victims. (District 4) More than 13,800 mu of farmland were flooded, with more than 7,200 disaster victims. (District 5) A total of more than 106,300 mu of farmland were flooded, more than 1,800 houses were flooded, and there were approximately 46,970 disaster victims, with more than 30 deaths. (District 6) A total of more than 61,240 mu of farmland were flooded, with approximately 17,140 disaster victims. (District 7) A total of more than 40,000 mu of farmland were flooded, and approximately 2,000 houses were in the water, with approximately 9,000 disaster victims. In the seven districts above, a total of more than 281,200 mu of farmland were flooded, and there were more than 124,000 disaster victims. The severity of the disaster is rare.

Partial Reorganization of the Jiangsu National Arts Hall: Hu Pu'an, the director of the Jiangsu Provincial National Arts Hall, in order to focus on talent and reorganize the interior, has specially hired Wu Xingu, the general editor of the hall, as the hall's secretary, and hired Sun Shaojiang, the chairman of the board of directors, as the chief of affairs. Yangzhou 90

Many Died in the Wanfu Bridge Ferry Accident: The Construction Bureau suggested that due to the collapse of both the Wanfu Bridge and the Dongshi Bridge in Dongxiang, merchants should be recruited to undertake ferry services. It is now learned that the ferry service has not yet been contracted, and the original ferryboat suddenly encountered danger on the 7th at around 11:00 AM while sailing from Wanfu Bridge to Xian, due to the rapid tide and currents. More than 40 passengers were drowned, and their bodies drifted away with the waves, making it impossible to retrieve them.

After the Dam Was Opened, the Floodwater in Jiangdu Settled: The water level in the Grand Canal dropped by five inches on the 6th. The water level in the Jiangdu Fan San Gou Sluice Gate was two zhang three chi six cun. There was no rise on the 7th. The water discharge is underway, and there has been no retreat. On the 5th, the telegram stated that the water level at Yumatou was one zhang nine chi one cun. The provincial government has dispatched Qian Jia, the section chief of the Third Division, to reside in Gaoyou. He returned to the province from Yangzhou on the 7th to report. However, in the northern townships of Chi'an Lake, Gongdao Bridge, Songjia Bridge, Yangshou Dam, and Fangjia Lane, the embankments had previously been flooded due to the rise of the lake, submerging tens of thousands of acres of embanked fields. Four to five thousand residents, totaling 40,000 people, were all engulfed in water. Now that the dam has been opened and the water has receded, the houses are gone. In addition to the floating corpses of humans and livestock, the survivors are displaced and must still engage in the work of retrieving and burying the floating corpses. The situation is extremely tragic. Representatives have been sent out in all directions for relief. West of Shaobo, the wind is tight, and in addition to opening the five dams leading to the sea, it is no longer possible to open the central dam of Gaoyou and the Zhaoguan dam of Jiangdu. There is still concern that "when the west wind arrives, the riverbanks will collapse."

Discussion on the Plan to Protect the Shaobo Embankment from Danger: County Magistrate Chen Nanxuan, following the provincial government's telegram order that the embankment along the canal should be protected by the director in conjunction with the county magistrates, specially sent Section Chief Lu Shiquan to Shaobo to meet with Shao Fuchen, the director of the Jiangdu section of the Canal Works Office, to convene a meeting of various institutions and organizations in the town to discuss defense projects. The following emergency measures were agreed upon: (1) The director of the Shaobo office will be responsible for ordering the Jiangdu Fan to increase personnel stationed at the worksite every night. (2) Two thousand shi of firewood must be rushed, along with hemp bags, rush bags, and ropes, to Shaobo in preparation for emergency repairs. (3) The use of farmland for soil extraction should be started first, and after the project is completed, the district office, together with the works office, will evaluate the value and submit it to the province for distribution. It is reported that the people of Shaobo have already formed a defense team. The method is that the town criers will announce to the villagers that each household should send one able-bodied man with a lantern to gather at Tieniu Bay at night, with a total of about 500 people, to carry out patrol duties to prevent the embankment from collapsing and causing danger.

Nantong 91

The Difficulty in Recovering the Bodies from the Dahe Ship: The case of the bodies found on the Dahe ship, which caused a sensation throughout the county, was thoroughly investigated by the Zhenjiang District Court as designated by the High Court. The Zhenjiang Court sent a letter to the County Court, which forwarded it to the Nantong County Public Security Bureau, ordering the Tianshenggang Public Security Sub-bureau, which originally handled the case, to summon the body's nephew, Li Yifu, to the case to point out the location of the burial in order to send personnel to inspect. The new chief, Zhu Tingshi, found that there were no case files in the bureau, making it difficult to handle. It is unknown how to resolve the issue.

Bandit Activity Rises Again in the Eastern and Western Townships: Recently, bandits have infiltrated the Yiyu and other districts in the eastern townships of Nantong, causing great disturbances. Hangzhou 92

Suicide Note Due to Business Failure: Xiao Guangxian, a traveler from Baoqing, Hunan, 30 years old, residing in Room 17 of the Central Hotel on Yanling Road in the New Market of Hangzhou City, committed suicide after a business failure in Changsha. He arrived in Hangzhou on the 19th of last month via Shanghai and stayed at the hotel. He carried a suitcase and a mesh basket. After half a month, he had not paid any room fees. Feeling the pain of economic pressure, he suddenly had the desire to die. At around 2:00 AM the night before, he took advantage of the lack of preparation and wrote a suicide note, detailing the reasons for his suicide and his hardships, stating that the clothes and luggage should be used to pay for the room and board, and that a wristwatch should be given to the tea boy, etc. He then hanged himself from the bed railing with a belt. At 9:00 AM on the 8th, the tea boy saw the scene and was greatly shocked. He rushed to release the body, but it was too late. The person had already died. He immediately reported to the police station. Due to the hot weather, the body was starting to smell. At 2:00 PM in the afternoon, the Hangzhou District Court sent personnel to inspect and confirmed that the cause of death was suicide by hanging. The court then filled out the forms and arranged for a coffin and burial.

Opening Ceremony of the Newspaper Exhibition: The opening ceremony of the Newspaper Exhibition organized by the Hangzhou Society of the Chinese Society of Newspaper Studies was held at 2:00 PM yesterday (the 8th). More than 100 guests and participants attended. The exhibition rooms were located in the classrooms of the West Lake Art Academy. There were no fewer than ten thousand kinds of old and new newspapers. A group photo was taken, and the meeting adjourned. In the evening, the summer training institute of the society held a party.

Car Collision Injures Passengers: At a relatively quiet place near the Pinghai Bridge on Pinghai Road in Hangzhou City, at around 12:00 AM on the night of the 7th, a black cat company's car number 284, carrying passengers, was returning from Bi Jiao Fang, unexpectedly another car numbered 233 of the Daye Company, driven by a driver named Zhou Eun, traveling at high speed from Dong Wansha Road, collided with the Black Cat car. Both sides were damaged, and passenger Wang Desheng was injured in the head and sent to the Tongren Hospital for treatment. The two drivers were detained by the police for interrogation.

Shaoxing 93

Agreed Plan for Silver and Rice Disaster Relief: Shaoxing silver and rice, in recent years, has been collected less and less, and the deficits are extremely abnormal. Now, the provincial treasury is empty, and there is an urgent need for collection. The Finance Department has commissioned Shen Weiwen to come to Shaoxing to supervise the urging. He has now agreed on relief measures together with the county bureau, ordering Zhou Deyuan, the director of the Field Tax Collection Office, to collect 95,000 taels of new grain and 12,000 dan of rice from the 20th year of the Republic within the stipulated one-year period, as well as 50,000 taels of old grain and 4,000 dan of rice from previous years. The above are the minimum amounts, and a guarantee has been invited. If there are delays, the director will be responsible for compensating. Extra expenses required will be subsidized at a rate of 7 cents per yuan to supplement.

Xiaoshan 94

Police Destroy Road Construction Site: He Jintao and other policemen from the Xiaoshan County Public Security Bureau were playing on the handcar of the Xiaojian section of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Road on the 3rd of this month, which led to a conflict with the road workers. That night, the police, armed with guns, went to the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Road construction site and destroyed it. The matter escalated. It is reported that the construction site has also submitted the torn charts and other items to the headquarters for record. The road workers are still unwilling to let the matter rest.

Panic Caused by a Mad Soldier's False Report of Passing Soldiers: At 10:00 PM on the night of the 4th in Xiaoshan City, the lights suddenly went out in all places, and the stores on the main streets closed. At the same time, police sirens blared. A mad soldier shouted that thousands of defeated soldiers were passing through the city, causing the merchants and residents in the urban area to panic and flee in all directions, as if a major disaster was imminent. After an hour, there was no movement, and people's hearts began to settle. The mad soldier then reported to the police station. After being questioned by the Public Security Bureau, the mad soldier's words were incoherent, and it was discovered that he had a mental illness. The soldier was arrested and sent to the provincial government on the 5th for investigation.

Government and Merchants Maintain People's Food Supply 97

Rice Industry Price Limit Not to Exceed 17 Yuan

The Social Affairs Bureau Orders to Prohibit Hoarding: Seeing that rice prices have been rising continuously in recent days, which is not entirely due to the relationship between supply and demand, the Social Affairs Bureau has issued separate orders to the guild associations of the bean and rice industries, etc.: In order to comply with orders, it is found that rice prices have been rising due to water obstacles in shipping routes, and Ding geng has reached 18 yuan. It is important to know that geng rice had a bumper harvest last autumn, and the production area has rich reserves this year, which are enough to use when the season is running out, although disaster relief rice is needed in various places. However, it is limited to Xianyang rice. Geng rice is still in the midst of a ban on exports. Why do you raise the price so high to hinder the people's food supply? Therefore, this order is issued to the guild association, and you are to quickly notify your peers that there must be no more hoarding or manipulating of prices, resulting in disaster. This order, etc.

Bean and Rice Industry Discussed Price Limit: The guild associations of the bean and rice industries in this city recently received an order from the Social Affairs Bureau to order their peers not to take the opportunity to raise grain prices, etc. Therefore, yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, a general meeting of all peers was convened in Cuixiu Hall to discuss the instructions from the Social Affairs Bureau. Everyone believed that the continuous rain this time, the scarcity of sources, and the soaring rice prices were all due to the times, but in order to maintain the people's food supply, the highest white keng rice should not exceed 17 yuan per stone, and the middle and second grades should be priced separately. It is reported that the industry has been notified to comply and has reported to the Social Affairs Bureau for filing.

Yesterday

Chung Hwa Book Company Suspends Operations 98

The Social Affairs Bureau Ordered Resumption of Operations Yesterday

Board of Directors Resolved to Resume Work Tomorrow

Because the Publishing Industry Workers' Union held a general meeting to establish a branch office of the union at the Chung Hwa Book Company's branch office at 4 PM the day before yesterday (the 7th), which was deemed an illegal action, the Chung Hwa Book Company urgently telegraphed that evening to temporarily suspend operations starting yesterday, pending an on-site inspection by the authorities. The Publishing Industry Workers' Union considered this an act of suppressing the labor movement and requested a severe punishment. The Social Affairs Bureau strictly ordered the cessation of the suspension of operations. The Chung Hwa Book Company held a board meeting last night to discuss solutions. The details of the situation are recorded below:

Telegram Announcing Suspension of Operations: Chung Hwa Book Company urgently telegraphed a temporary suspension of operations, stating: To the Nanjing Central Political Conference, Central Party Headquarters, National Government, Executive Yuan, Ministry of Industry, Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters, Mayor, Social Affairs Bureau, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and Book Industry Guild: At 3 PM on the afternoon of the 6th of this month, the Shanghai Publishing Industry Workers' Union sent a letter stating that a branch office of the Publishing Industry Workers' Union would be established at the Chung Hwa Book Company at 4 PM on the afternoon of the 7th, requesting to end work one and a half hours early. We immediately replied, stating that the letter did not specify which department, and requested clear instructions to submit to the board of directors, etc., and reported it to the Municipal Party Headquarters and Social Affairs Bureau for record. Unexpectedly, at 3 PM on the afternoon of the 7th, fifty to sixty people suddenly broke into the workshops, monitoring the workers' actions, locking the front and back doors, and prohibiting entry and exit. At 4 PM, someone who identified himself as Zhu Yuansong, claiming to have been sent by Mr. Wang Wenhua, rang the work stoppage bell without authorization, forcing workers to attend the meeting. At the same time, many people went to the general office and editorial department, forcibly locking the doors and expelling the editors and office workers to the open space. Staff and workers could not go out or enter the workshops. In the evening, there was almost a conflict before the doors were opened and the meeting was dismissed. It was found that the unauthorized ringing of the work stoppage bell at 4 PM was sudden, interrupting work, and the disturbance by many people caused disorder. Xin Cheng, Xie Tai, Xi San, and others were present and were at a loss. Many employees visited at night, saying that in this situation, human rights were not guaranteed, and freedom was being deprived, requesting the company to find a solution, otherwise everyone would be in danger. Article 20 of the Trade Union Law stipulates that trade unions shall not force workers to join, and Article 27 stipulates that trade union officials or members shall not close shops or factories. The union's actions are so illegal that the company's property and business, and the employees' lives and freedom, have lost their protection. As a last resort, operations will be temporarily suspended tomorrow, and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and Municipal Chamber of Commerce will be requested to send personnel for on-site inspection to seek administrative and legal remedies. Urgent words, hoping for consideration. Respectfully, Lu Fei Kui, General Manager of Chung Hwa Book Company Limited, Shu Xincheng, Director of the Editorial Department, Chen Xietai, Director of the Printing Department, and Lu Xisan, Director of the General Office.

Union Notice: The Municipal Publishing Industry Workers' Union urgently notified all members, stating: The Chung Hwa Book Company office of this union held a general meeting of members at 4 PM yesterday. Representatives from the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Government Social Affairs Bureau attended to provide guidance. The legal procedures were extremely complete. However, the management of the company is cunning and rogue, making false statements to create alarm, and has arbitrarily suspended operations, resorting to the old tricks of suppressing the labor movement from 1927, in order to intimidate workers. Their intention is nothing more than to undermine the union organization. In addition to submitting a request to the Municipal Government Social Affairs Bureau for strict sanctions, the city has also sent a letter directly to the management, urging them to realize their mistake and resume work immediately. All wages during the suspension period should be paid in full by the management. All members, please rest assured and strengthen unity. The union will fulfill its responsibility to fully protect you. This is announced.

Ministry of Industry's Telegram Inquiry: The main factory, branch printing factory, general office, and editorial department of Chung Hwa Book Company on Jing'an Temple Road implemented a suspension of operations starting yesterday. More than a thousand employees were out of work. Yesterday afternoon, a telegram was received from the Ministry of Industry, stating: Chung Hwa Book Company, your telegram is noted. The Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has been telegraphed to investigate and handle it properly according to law. Special reply, Ministry of Industry.

Management Petition: Yesterday morning, Lu Fei Bohong, General Manager of Chung Hwa Book Company, and Shu Xincheng, Director of the Translation Department, personally went to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to report the suspension of operations and requested that personnel be sent for on-site inspection. Director Pan Gongzhan received them and accepted the request. At the same time, Lu Xisan and Chen Xietai were sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to request that personnel be sent for investigation. Committee members Ye Huijun and Lu Fengzhu received them and accepted the request. In the afternoon, the Social Affairs Bureau sent Zhu Jintao to investigate thoroughly for review. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent Ye Huijun and Lu Fengzhu to investigate for submission.

Social Affairs Bureau Order: The Social Affairs Bureau yesterday ordered Chung Hwa Book Company to continue normal operations, stating: An order to comply. According to advertisements in today's local newspapers, if the trade union has illegal actions, it should be reported to this bureau for investigation. Arbitrarily suspending operations affects the livelihood of all employees, which is inappropriate. You are hereby ordered to comply and must resume normal operations tomorrow and await this bureau's review. Do not delay. This order is imperative.

Board Meeting: Chung Hwa Book Company held a board meeting at the general distribution office on Simar Road at 3 PM yesterday. All directors, including Lu Fei Bohong, and senior officials, such as Shu Xincheng, Director of the Editorial Department, Chen Xietai, Director of the Printing Department, Wang Jinshi, Deputy Director, and Lu Xisan, Director of the General Office, were present. It was decided on the spot that work would resume on Monday in compliance with the order, and the authorities would be awaited to review. An advertisement would be placed in newspapers immediately to announce this.

Book Industry Meeting: The Book Industry Guild held an emergency meeting at 5 PM yesterday. More than twenty people, including Lu Fei Bohong, attended to discuss the Chung Hwa Book Company suspension case. A telegram was sent, stating: To Commander-in-Chief Jiang in Nanchang, the Central Party Headquarters in Nanjing, the Central Political Conference, the Executive Yuan of the National Government, and the Ministry of Industry: According to the telegram report from member Chung Hwa Book Company (details omitted from the previous text), after the guild investigated and verified, the sudden stoppage of power in the Chung Hwa Book Company factory caused significant losses. Moreover, the Publishing Industry Workers' Union disregarded the provisional law, criminal law, and trade union law, trampled on human rights, undermined industry, and did not adhere to the scope of its mission. If this trend continues, government laws will be treated as trash, and the future of industry and commerce will be unthinkable. We request a thorough investigation and punishment to fulfill the last wishes of the late Premier to revitalize industry and save the country. Before this matter is resolved according to law, the Book Industry Guild of Shanghai will not recognize any actions taken by the Publishing Industry Workers' Union towards other bookstores. Respectfully, Shanghai Book Industry Guild.

Union Condolences: The Publishing Industry Workers' Union has reportedly scheduled a general meeting of representatives from various unions to discuss countermeasures. The Water and Electricity Industry Union and other unions visited the union yesterday to express their condolences and offered to serve as a backing.

Chamber of Commerce Statement: The Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Industry and the municipal party and government agencies yesterday regarding the Chung Hwa Book Company's suspension of operations, stating: Chung Hwa Book Company did not reject the Publishing Industry Workers' Union's request to end work one and a half hours early. If the time was too short, the union could have sent representatives to contact the responsible personnel of the company after receiving the company's reply, either to end work early for all or for a part. All have its proper procedure to follow. If the company did not accept, the union should have appealed to the party and government agencies according to law for sanctions. However, the union did not consider these measures and led many people to act violently. Locking the front and back doors, prohibiting entry and exit, directly blockaded the factory, violating the prohibition in Article 27, Paragraph 1, of the Trade Union Law. The unauthorized ringing of the work stoppage bell and forcing workers to attend the meeting was done without prior solicitation of membership and intended to force all workers of the company to join the union, violating the prohibition in Article 20 of the Trade Union Law. To achieve harmonious labor-management relations, it is necessary to strictly adhere to national laws and regulations and to understand each other in case of incidents. If they rely on their numbers and strength to act outside the bounds of law, then boundaries will be difficult to eliminate, industry will be difficult to develop, and it will only open the door to instigation by treacherous people, which is a hidden worry for the future of the country and social order. It is appropriate to report the situation to your ministry and bureau for review and to grant sanctions according to law so that the company can receive the legal protection it deserves, which is in the public interest. Respectfully, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

Union Letter: The Publishing Industry Workers' Union sent a letter to the General Manager of Chung Hwa Book Company yesterday, stating: Dear Mr. Bohong, Upon reading the front-page advertisement in various newspapers, the content of your company's urgent telegram is absurd. Its false statements and alarmist rhetoric clearly intend to undermine workers joining the union. It is regrettable that a leading cultural institution in the country disregards law and reason and resorts to such a low tactic. According to the meeting procedure, the Municipal Party Headquarters and Social Affairs Bureau sent official representatives to guide the meeting on site and witnessed the actual situation. The Political Department of the Public Concession also sent investigator Li Haifeng to maintain order. However, your company groundlessly claims that the property, business, employees' lives, and freedom have lost their protection. Your company cannot hide the truth from the world. The union does not wish to argue further on this point. However, the union disapproves of your company's old tricks of suspending operations for three months in 1927 to suppress the labor movement. The union has always maintained consistent labor-management relations and cannot refrain from offering the following sincere advice. We hope that your company can have a full understanding and resume operations as usual. In the future, we can discuss the welfare of both parties in the long term. Otherwise, if this causes more serious disputes, your company should bear full responsibility.

Union Defense: The Publishing Industry Workers' Union submitted a report to the Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Party Headquarters yesterday, stating: Requesting an order for Chung Hwa Book Company to resume operations immediately to promote the labor movement and maintain industry. The members of the Chung Hwa Book Company requested to convene a general meeting of the Shanghai Publishing Industry Workers' Union Chung Hwa Book Company branch office at the Chung Hwa Book Company's main factory at 4 PM on August 7, which has been reported to your bureau for review and approval, and representatives were sent to provide guidance. Unexpectedly, Lu Fei Kui, General Manager of the company, Shu Xincheng, Director of the Translation Department, Chen Xietai, Director of the Printing Department, and Lu Xisan, Director of the General Office, advertised the company's urgent telegram in the local newspapers on August 8 (details omitted). According to the investigation, the meeting was convened at 4 PM on August 7, and the general manager of the company was officially notified in advance. During the meeting, representatives Gu Bingyuan from your bureau and Wu Jiazhe from the Municipal Party Headquarters provided guidance. All procedures were handled in accordance with the initial steps of civil rights. However, the company's management dared to fabricate facts and falsely claim that the union forced workers to join and blockaded the company's factory. Ask if there was such behavior that day. The representatives from your bureau will have a report to prove, and the union does not need to defend itself. The company's management arbitrarily suspended operations, used its old tricks, suppressed the labor movement, and opposed the members of the union. The facts are clear and cannot be denied. We respectfully request that the company be ordered to resume operations immediately and publish a correction of the false information in the telegram to promote the labor movement and maintain industry, which is in the public interest.

Management Submission: Chung Hwa Book Company submitted a document to the Social Affairs Bureau, stating: To request the distinction between the nature of trade unions to comply with. On August 6, at 3 PM, a letter was received from the Shanghai Publishing Workers' Union, stating (details omitted). According to Article 2 of the Trade Union Law, a union organized by workers of different occupations within the same enterprise is an industrial union, and a union organized by workers of the same occupation is a professional union. In the past, the company had an internal industrial Chung Hwa Book Company Union, and there were external professional bookbinding unions, color printing unions, ink lithography unions, and lead printing unions. The store clerks are also members of the Bookstore Guild, Color Printing Industry Guild, and Instrument and Stationery Guild. Now there is an industrial and professional Publishing Industry Union, leaving the company and workers at a loss as to what to do. If the Trade Union Law and its implementing regulations are studied carefully, the Chung Hwa Book Company, except for the staff and clerks' union organized four years ago, which has been legally canceled, the Chung Hwa Book Company Printing Factory Union is an industrial union, and the bookbinding union, etc., are professional unions. Choose one of the two to retain and strictly prohibit double union membership to avoid diverging methods and conflicting orders. This would benefit both commercial and labor movements and comply with the provisions of the Trade Union Law. We respectfully request instructions on how to proceed.
