Chen Shaokuan's Remarks After Arriving in Shanghai 101

Detained Aircraft Parts Can Be Resolved Soon

Chen Jiliang Is Scheduled to Go to Fujian Tomorrow

Du Xigui Is Suffering from Severe Diarrhea

Naval Vice Minister Chen Shaokuan arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday. A reporter from the East China News Agency interviewed him at the Jiangnan Shipyard yesterday. According to him:

Detained Aircraft Parts: Regarding the customs detention of aircraft parts, I believe there is no major issue. Although the parts shipped from abroad by the Jiangnan Shipyard have passports, they are often delayed by the Jianghai Customs for a period of time before they can be picked up. Therefore, the aircraft parts are no exception. It can be resolved in about one or two days. In the past, when purchasing imported parts, if the customs mistakenly believed that taxes were required, the ministry could only pay first as a guarantee, and then the tax would be refunded after the customs verified that they were tax-exempt items. The funds required by the ministry are allocated by the Ministry of Finance, so paying taxes is just a more cumbersome procedure.

Chen's Trip to Fujian: Commander Chen Jiliang of the First Fleet is scheduled to go to Fujian next Monday. All personnel of the department have moved to the Hai Rong warship. The headquarters of the first team will be stationed on the ship. The Hai Chou and other eight ships will sail to the exercises at the same time.

Du Is Sick: General Du Xigui, the newly appointed president of the Mawei Naval Academy, was originally scheduled to go to Fujian next month to take office, but he suddenly felt the heat due to the hot weather the day before yesterday and is now suffering from severe diarrhea. General Du is old and physically weak. He is now being treated by a Western doctor. I visited him personally yesterday.

Li Shijia Returns: As for Li Shijia, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Navy, who was ordered to go to Japan to inspect students and inspect the Ninghai ship project, has completed his mission and is scheduled to return to China next week. Due to financial difficulties, it is feared that this year's graduates from the Naval Aviation Department will not be able to study abroad.

Anti-Japanese Association Warns Unscrupulous Merchants 106

Severe Sanctions Will Be Imposed If Smuggling Continues

Chamber of Commerce Urges Chinese Yarn Merchants Not to Raise Prices Opportunistically

According to the New Voice Society, since the incident of Korean people discriminating against Chinese people, the Chinese people seem to have awakened somewhat. The work of the Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Committee is also not as it used to be. However, some unscrupulous merchants are still smuggling Japanese goods and taking the opportunity to raise prices. The following is a record of the committee's warning to various merchants and the meeting of the Custody Section yesterday.

Warning Against Smuggling: Yesterday, the association sent letters of warning to customs brokers such as Sin Chong Loong, Sin Chong Guan, Jardine Yü, Taikoo Fai, Fu Wo, Da Chuan Tong, Fai Kee, and Yat Sang Yü, as well as Hong Da Cheung and Yu Hong Cheung, two stores dealing in foreign seafood. The letter stated: "It has been verified that your company is smuggling Japanese goods in an attempt to profit from them. During this incident where Japanese people cruelly murdered overseas Chinese, all those with blood and spirit deeply hate this. All circles in the city of Yu initiated a fervent movement of economic severance with Japan, vowing to fight to the death with a spirit of non-cooperation. Yet your company dares to defy public opinion and smuggle Japanese goods, not only willingly acting as the ringleader in destroying the anti-Japanese movement, but also making yourselves public enemies of the entire nation. This has been decided upon after deliberation by the Sixth Standing Committee Meeting of this association, and a severe warning is hereby issued. If it is discovered that you are outwardly compliant but inwardly resistant, then public opinion will naturally impose severe sanctions. We hope you will think twice."

Prohibition of Price Hikes for Chinese Yarn: The City Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Chinese Yarn Factory Association, stating: "On the 7th of this month, we received a letter from the Jiangyin County Chamber of Commerce stating, 'Our county's textile industry has always relied on Japanese yarn factories in Shanghai for raw materials. During this boycott movement, if there is no solution for the aforementioned cotton yarn, there is concern that the domestic dyeing and weaving industry will face unemployment. However, Chinese yarn factories in Shanghai are taking advantage of the opportunity to drastically increase the price by 30 to 40 taels per piece. We believe that when the Chinese people are subjected to the humiliation and oppression of Japanese imperialism, the entire nation is united, bearing sorrow and pain, and embracing great sacrifices to carry out the boycott movement. Yet, Chinese yarn factories are taking advantage of the opportunity to profit, raising yarn prices, which is no different from destroying the boycott movement, causing the dyeing and weaving industry to suffer. Considering the matter logically, how can this be considered fair? We are writing to request that you forward this to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Committee to stop Chinese yarn factories from taking the opportunity to raise prices, and to sell all brands of cotton yarn at the prices before the boycott movement. Chinese yarn factories should be able to clarify their intentions. We are very eager for this outcome.' We approve of this. The boycott movement should be nationwide. However, the Chinese yarn factories are taking advantage of the opportunity to raise yarn prices, which is greatly detrimental to domestic industry. We approve of the reasons in the letter. In addition to forwarding this, we are writing to inform you and hope that you will investigate and correct this promptly to rectify the city's atmosphere and maintain the industry." The letter arrived at the association. The letter also said that, "This economic severance with Japan is an opportunity for Chinese yarn to sell well. Even if you consider the business itself, selling at the same price as before the boycott, the profits are already considerable. If you take the opportunity to raise prices again, the dyeing and weaving industries everywhere will suffer greatly. It's not a method that takes public welfare into consideration. We are writing to request that your association earnestly advise the yarn factories among your members to sell at the same price as before the boycott, in order to maintain the weaving industry (in the spirit of public friendship)."

Meeting of the Custody Section: The Custody Section of the association held its second section meeting at 3:00 PM yesterday in the meeting room. Zhang Yichen, Wang Yansong (represented by Tian Siwei), Zhou Ganling, Dong Jianfeng, Fan Chuchen, Zhang Xiankang, Fu Yaoqing, Gu Shanzhang, Sun Sijiu, and Tian Siwei attended. Zhang Yichen chaired and Gu Shanzhang recorded. The meeting opened with formalities. After the chairman and various secretaries reported, the discussion began: (1) Regarding the proposal to rent another warehouse in the Nanshi area to store additional items and facilitate storage, the resolution was passed. (2) Regarding Gu Shanzhang's request to the secretariat to send a letter to the Public Security Bureau to increase patrols in the cargo depots in various districts and to dispatch police assistance when necessary, the resolution was passed. (3) Regarding Zhou Ganling's proposal that the section should rent a large warehouse in a convenient location for transportation as a general cargo depot for storing large batches of whole pieces of goods, the resolution was passed. (4) Regarding the re-establishment of the date for the section meeting, the resolution was passed for every Sunday afternoon at 3:00 PM. Other matters were briefly discussed.

Assault Has Been Compensated: On July 27th, Zhong Jinghan and Cai Peiyuan, employees of Shen Da Transportation Company, were arrested by the Public Security Bureau and sent to the Shanghai District Court for investigation for assaulting inspectors of the Anti-Japanese Association. It is now learned that the prosecutor of the court has persuaded the victims to request the withdrawal of the original case. As for Zhong Jinghan and Cai Peiyuan, because they were apprehended for committing assault, they voluntarily compensated for medical expenses and apologized in person. It is said that the Anti-Japanese Association has informally indicated that it will not pursue the matter deeply because the perpetrators have admitted their mistake, apologized, and compensated for the losses. This matter may come to an end here.

Insult Has Been Apologized For: Xin Tai Chang Trading Company of the Sixteenth Section of Nanshi was detained by the Nanshi Inspection Office of the Inspection Section of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Association because it transported five hemp sacks. After the association verified that the hemp sacks were not Japanese goods, the Standing Committee decided to release them. While the office was following the procedures to order the Nanshi Inspection Office to release the goods, Ying Dingsheng, a partner of the trading company, rushed to the Inspection Section of the Anti-Japanese Association, making trouble unreasonably, being imposing, speaking rudely, and cursing wildly. The incident was heard by all the staff of the association and caused great indignation. Everyone believed that Ying Dingsheng's public insult should be punished appropriately as a warning. Lin Yuanqing and others from the trading company repeatedly pleaded on his behalf, forgiving his first offense and exempting him from prosecution. It is said that the association, as an organization of patriotic movement, has been making every effort to protect domestic goods. If there are any suspicious goods, they will be temporarily detained. Once it is verified that they are domestic goods, they will be returned immediately. Ying Dingsheng knew that he was in the wrong for his rude words and immediately apologized to the staff of the Anti-Japanese Association. Xin Tai Chang Trading Company will also publish an apology in the newspaper.

Municipal Government Order

Abolition of Four Labor Regulations 107

The Shanghai Municipal Government, as the Factory Law and its implementing regulations have been promulgated by the Central Government, has specifically ordered the abolition of the following four single regulations of the city: "Shanghai Municipal Employee Retirement Treatment Provisional Measures," "Shanghai Municipal Employee Treatment Provisional Rules," "Shanghai Municipal Employee Service Provisional Rules," and "Shanghai Municipal Apprentice Provisional Rules," to avoid conflicts with the central government's orders.

Feng Liutang Talks

The Food Situation Amid the Flood 108

There Are No Major Concerns This Year

Preparation Should Be Made Urgently for the Future

Recently, various rice-producing areas have reported floods and damage to crops, causing public anxiety and a gradual increase in rice prices. A reporter from the Wuchen Society visited Mr. Feng Liutang, Chairman of the Food Committee of the Social Affairs Bureau, yesterday to inquire about the food situation in the future. Mr. Feng provided a general overview, stating,

The Food Supply of This City: Has always relied on transportation from various regions. Those coming from north of Shanghai mainly come from Changshu, Wuxi, Chengqing. Those arriving from south of Shanghai mostly come from the Songjiang and Wuxian areas. Since last year's bumper harvest, the storage of factories in Wuxi and other places is still abundant, with signs of surplus. Even landlords and rural farmers in the interior, aware of the high rice prices in the past two years, and those who are capable, are thinking of selling when the price is right. Therefore, the current rice reserves should be sufficient to meet the current needs, so it seems that there should be no problems. Moreover, new japonica rice from Pudong has been on the market for four or five days. Although the quantity is limited, the arrival of new rice should slightly weaken psychological factors. After this month, Dongxin rice will be in full bloom, and the arrival of Xixin rice is not far away.

The Key for the Future: Lies in whether the weather can be sunny and rainy in moderation, and without hurricanes. The disaster of this flood was particularly light in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. The fields along the lake and swamps are certainly hopeless. However, it is difficult to have three or four years of harvest for this type of field rice in ten years. However, due to the excessive amount of water this year, Lu Xian rice will inevitably suffer the same damage. However, if the weather is favorable, the major fields of rice can still have a harvest of 50 to 60%, which depends on fate and is not controlled by human power.

Disasters in Various Regions: According to reports, all rice-producing areas have suffered from major floods, especially the Hunan and Anhui provinces, which are most closely related to the people's food. Anhui rice (commonly known as Ke Xian) is concentrated in Wuhu and can be transshipped to various provinces. Therefore, the damage to Anhui rice has the same impact on the food of various provinces. This time, most of the rice-producing areas in Anhui Province were flooded, and the poor harvest is expected. In previous years, when the grain supply was insufficient between the old and new harvests, Anhui rice, which came out earlier, could be used to adjust the situation. It is difficult to predict whether there will be such hope this year. Hunan and Hubei provinces have always been famous for producing rice. There is a saying that "If Hunan and Hubei are ripe, the world is sufficient. If Wujiang is ripe, there is only a bowl of porridge." However, the floods in Hunan and Hubei are unusually severe. According to recent news, if the weather in Hunan Province clears up and the water recedes quickly, there may still be 40 to 50% of harvest. Recently, there has been an order prohibiting rice from leaving the province. The harvest of Li rice is affected by bandits and communists, so it cannot be fully guaranteed. During the early Qing Dynasty, Sichuan Province often transported grain to supply the provinces in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River. In recent years, there have been imports of foreign rice, and grain production has decreased, which can be seen from this. However, since various places have suffered from floods and the fields and houses have been damaged, even if there is any remedy,

Famine in the Future: Is already unavoidable. What is important now is urgent relief, and we should also pay attention to the future food supply, otherwise, a panic like that of 1930 will occur again, or even worse. Competing to purchase foreign rice will only increase the leakage of resources. However, according to China's current situation, it is necessary to drink poison to quench thirst, that is, to adopt the method of purchasing foreign rice. However, there should also be a way to purchase foreign rice. For example, this time, the price of foreign rice has been reported to be rising. It is said that a certain foreign firm added to the flood and insect disasters in China, and immediately telegraphed to Siam and Annam, where rice is produced, to order tens of thousands of tons. The market price has soared. Chinese merchants do not have direct dealings with foreign countries and are at their mercy. In the future, if various provinces are in famine, and compete to purchase foreign rice, it will give people the opportunity to manipulate and hoard, and we will only suffer unnecessary losses. Therefore, even if we want to purchase foreign rice in the future, it is best to be prepared, be able to communicate with each other, and not raise grain prices due to sudden supply and demand relations. To be able to absorb foreign rice from a more profitable way, then the reduction of this loss is also considerable, which depends on the cooperation of the provinces and cities and the merchants who purchase foreign rice, or it can be realized. Currently,

The Most Important Work: Is to understand how severe the disaster is in various rice-producing areas, which is closely related to the relief of the famine in the future. If the percentage of the disaster and the approximate amount of the autumn harvest can be accurately investigated by the disaster relief personnel in various places this time, then after this change, the county governments of each place will supervise the villages and townships to investigate and report at any time until the autumn harvest is completed. This percentage and approximate amount must be as close to the actual situation as possible. Report to the Ministry of Interior and announce it to various places. In order to cope with this famine, a united agency should be established by the producing and selling provinces and cities to make overall plans and cooperate, so that the purchase and distribution of food can have a basis and not be blindly moved, and its benefits will be even greater. However, in the past, provinces and cities often

Prohibited Transportation and Curtailed Purchase: This method can be maintained for a while, but if everyone follows suit, the circulation of food will lose its freedom, and there will inevitably be those who suffer from it. Therefore, mutual circulation is still appropriate. If one place prohibits transportation out of the country, and it is unknown whether it can be self-sufficient after the prohibition, if another place is short of food, it will retaliate in the same way. The danger is great. Moreover, if it is possible to export high-priced rice and buy cheap rice, it will benefit the food economy of the area. Why must we be in the same country, with borders like the states of Qin and Yue looking at each other? We must know that the food problem is a whole, and it can only be solved through cooperation. Dealing with it piecemeal will not help. As for the future price of rice, it may be influenced by the rush to purchase relief rice in various places, and the public's heart will be strong and prices will gradually rise. It is also possible. However, japonica rice is prohibited from leaving the country and has a large amount of reserves, so there should not be as drastic a situation as last year. Xian rice will inevitably be taken high, and it is inevitable. The Social Affairs Bureau is paying attention to the food supply at any time. Since the registration of foreign rice, the import and export of rice in this city has become clearer. Even with the increase in rice prices, although it contains seasonality and flood, the Social Affairs Bureau has ordered the rice merchants not to take the opportunity to raise prices, and when necessary, appropriate measures will be taken. However, what will happen to the rice market after the new harvest? If there is no way to make overall plans, Shanghai will inevitably face great difficulties.

The Flour Industry: Over the years, 50 to 60% of the raw materials have been dependent on the United States and Australia. The reason for this is the decline in the variety of domestic wheat. A peck of American wheat weighs 205.5 pounds. Australian wheat is white and the seeds are thick. A peck of Australian wheat weighs 206 pounds. A peck of Chinese wheat weighs only 166 pounds. Its weight is 39.5 pounds lighter than American wheat and 40 pounds lighter than Australian wheat. If the three types of wheat are placed together, as long as you pick the one that is withered and dirty, you can tell that it is Chinese wheat. The degradation of wheat production to such an extent is disheartening. In addition, when selling and transporting, farmers and vendors add mud and sand to increase the weight and seek improper profits. It is no wonder that flour mills are willing to buy foreign wheat and not domestic wheat. If this continues, domestic wheat will be completely eliminated one day. When that day comes, all the clothing, food, housing, and transportation of the Chinese people can be said to be completely westernized, and the China of China can be imagined. Although there was an inspection of wheat in the past, it was only in name. Recently, the Shanghai Grain Trade Association has taken the initiative to carry out the improvement of wheat production, distributing American and Australian wheat seeds to grain industries in various producing areas across the country before the sowing season for farmers to try planting. It is said that several places in Jiangsu have sown Australian wheat and have achieved considerable results. The industry also started its own wheat inspection on the 1st of this month. If the management is proper, and it is considered to be promoted in various places, Shanghai grain merchants have gradually looked further in recent years and have been able to make a big splash. If they can uphold this spirit and persevere, and the government can maintain supervision, and all parties can provide assistance, there may be a glimmer of hope for the future of the people's food.

The Flour and Wheat Market: Has now lost its autonomy and is completely following the price of gold and the American and Australian wheat market. Recalling the time before and after the outbreak of the European War, Chinese flour was one of the main export products. Today, it is like this, and one cannot help but feel the difference between the past and the present. The worst thing for our flour industry is the dumping of foreign flour. There is Russian flour in the north and American flour in the west. Although the use of foreign wheat by the factory damages our agriculture and squeezes our country's wealth, the labor and capital are still paid by our Chinese people. If it is foreign flour, then what we get is only the meager profit of selling. Moreover, the result of dumping is that Chinese flour mills have no room to stand, and the damage will be immeasurable. As for the method of prevention, we can only invigorate ourselves and actively improve from the food production to seek self-sufficiency. Before we can be completely self-sufficient, we should also inspect the country's supply and demand situation for imported food and impose appropriate restrictions on tariffs at any time. The association has repeatedly suggested this, but it has not yet been realized. As for the future flour and wheat market, it depends on whether the American intention to lend wheat to Germany, as reported the day before, is realized. After it is realized, how will Germany dispose of the wheat? Will it still resell it at the same amount, or will it be processed into flour and sold? On one hand, we need to see how Russia's goal of dumping wheat abroad is. In short, since all the raw materials for China's flour industry are sought abroad, the profits obtained are ultimately meager. Recently, due to the rising water level of the Jiangbei Canal and the opening of the dams for discharge, the wheat-producing areas have been flooded again, resulting in a recent increase of three or four cents in the price of domestic wheat.

Investigation of Rumors About Extending the Concession 109

It Was Decided That the Public Security and Social Affairs Bureaus Should Investigate Together

The Method of Handling Will Be Determined After a Report Is Received

After all parties expressed their unanimous opposition to the rumors of expanding the concession in western Shanghai, the legitimate merchants and residents in western Shanghai also unanimously denied it. However, the Putong-Songjiang District Municipal Committee and the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession requested the municipal authorities to conduct a thorough investigation to punish the cunning and clarify the truth. Women's Relief Association Established Yesterday 110

The Shanghai Women's Relief Association held its inaugural meeting at the Junior Evangelism Corps in Xiaoximen at 3:00 PM yesterday. At around 9:00 AM, the preparatory committee members of the association hired a car to travel to various places in Nanshi and Zhabei to distribute propaganda slogans in order to expand publicity. Therefore, more than 500 members of the association and women from various groups attended the meeting in the afternoon, which was a grand occasion in the women's movement. The following is a summary of the main points:

Representatives Attending the Meeting: The male and female representatives who attended the meeting yesterday included Huang Zhaoxiong, representative of the Municipal Party Department; Chen Kecheng, representative of the Municipal Government; Sun Yongyi, representative of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau; Zhang Wenbo, representative of the Second Special District Court; Yang Pei, representative of the Municipal Education Bureau; Chu Huizhen, representative of the Women's Patriotic Goods Promotion Association; Zhu Jie, representative of the National Goods Exhibition Hall; and the Municipal Public Security Bureau Music Team.

Situation of the General Meeting: After the opening ceremony, Chairman Lin Kecong delivered the opening speech, and Huang Xiaoying reported on the preparatory process. Afterwards, guidance was provided by various institutions such as the Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Government. Finally, Ms. Tang Naixin delivered the reply. It was originally intended that the general meeting would elect the members of the general meeting on the same day. However, due to the lack of time, it was decided that the secretaries of each district would be elected first, and then the general meeting would be convened again to elect again. At that time, the original intention was reported by Sun Yongyi, the representative of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau.

Declaration of the General Meeting: The declaration of the general meeting was passed after three readings. Since the flag of the blue sky and white sun has illuminated Shenzhou, the oppressed women of our thousands of years have had a solid guarantee on the path of life. However, deeply rooted evil forces still exert their last lewd power, making you unable to hear with your ears, unable to see with your eyes, unable to move with your limbs, unable to express with your thoughts, let alone talk about obtaining freedom and enjoying equality. However, Rome was not built in a day. It is a dream to turn Moscow into Chicago overnight. The failure to liberate the majority of women cannot be attributed to the failure of the women's movement, but is actually a good medicine to promote the women's movement. The previous women's movement paid attention to active progress and neglected passive relief. As a result, the blessings of liberation only came to a small number of women, and the majority of compatriots are still sinking in the dark prison. If people are not concentrated, the strength will not be strong. If the strength is not strong, the cause will be difficult to achieve. This is originally the law of cause and effect, and the women's movement is no exception. Now, in order to save these mistakes and pave the way for future success, we must strive for passive relief at the same time as active progress, so that the largest and most painful compatriots can get rid of the shackles and see the light of day again, and then stand on a battle line and fight together to achieve the goal of equality between men and women. How to start the work of passive relief? Establish a women's relief association. The evil Shanghai is the nest of demons and the fortress of sin. Women are devastated by feudal forces and oppressed by imperialists. Therefore, painful groans can be heard everywhere, and desolate scenes can be seen at any time. Women are beaten by in-laws and husbands at home, and exploited by factory owners when they go out. The surroundings are either threats like tigers and wolves or poisonous temptations like snakes and scorpions. High-ranking women are insulted like toys, and low-ranking women are used like cattle and horses. Personality is lost, and the joy of life is completely gone. If they are not rescued as soon as possible, it is feared that there will be no women left in Shanghai, which is known as a city of three million people. This is the reason why the association is determined to establish itself as soon as possible. Women's relief work, in other words, is the work of overthrowing evil forces. However, evil forces have their history and their henchmen. It is difficult to achieve victory without a copper trunk and iron arms, wisdom, and good ways. Therefore, we women should be united, aim at the target, and rush forward in the spirit of the Prime Minister's fearlessness, kill all the enemies who oppress women, and ascend to the avenue of equality between men and women together.

Large Number of Aircraft Transported to Shanghai 111

Twenty Aircraft Shipped from the United States

Already in the Process of Extraction and Transportation

The Ministry of Military Affairs ordered military aircraft from the United States, including fighter planes and bombers, all of which are complete. The first shipment of 20 aircraft has been loaded from New York and San Francisco in the United States in two batches and transported to Shanghai. Yesterday, all of them were completely loaded. The aircraft are temporarily unloaded at the Pudong Wharf. The shipping company undertaking the loading has notified the Ministry of Military Affairs to prepare passports to come to Shanghai for extraction. Each of the American military aircraft transported this time costs US$30,000, totaling more than 2 million Shanghai dollars for 20 aircraft. The Ministry of Military Affairs has sent the transportation passports to Shanghai, and has entrusted a local trading company to handle the customs declaration. It is planned to be transported to Beijing for assembly by the Air Force team and then start test flights.

Wang Daji Accused 113

A Rickshaw Driver's Wife's Adultery 114

Eloping with Money and Clothes

Incited by Tang Fengming

Chen Bian-shi, the 22-year-old wife of Chen Jinbao, a rickshaw driver from Tongzhou residing at No. 60 Pingjili Road in the French Concession, absconded without a trace at 7 PM on the 3rd of this month, taking with her 600 yuan in cash, clothes, and a suitcase. Chen reported the incident to the police and requested an investigation. Chen discovered that Bian-shi was enticed by Tang Fengming from Hubei. On the evening of the 5th, Tang was found at No. 138 Ningkangli, Haining Road in the Public Concession. The police were notified and arrested Tang, sending him to the Huizi Police Station. The French Concession Police sent Detective Liu Youfa to No. 1463 Haining Road, where Bian-shi was arrested. 430 yuan in stolen cash, gold bracelets, watches, pawn tickets, and other items were confiscated and taken back to the French Concession Police Station. Yesterday, they were brought to the Second District Court for investigation. Judge Ge Zhitan of the Criminal Court, along with Prosecutor Lou Guangguang and Clerk Tao Zongkan, presided over the hearing. First, police lawyer Gu Shouxi presented the case, stating that the police were prosecuting based on Articles 256 and 337 of the Criminal Code, charging both incitement and theft, and requested an investigation. Plaintiff Chen Jinbao also submitted a complaint about his wife's abduction. Tang Fengming confessed that he met Bian-shi two years ago while playing mahjong. He claimed that Bian-shi left on her own accord and they met on Taipingqiao Road. She said she was upset because her husband was going to marry a concubine. She wanted to go out and go with him to a Henan hotel for three nights. On the sixth, Bian-shi rented a house herself, and he did not incite her. Chen Bian-shi confessed that her husband had an affair and often beat her, so she left. She met Tang on the road and stayed at a hotel. She left on her own accord and was not incited by Tang. She only took 500 yuan in cash, 300 yuan in banknotes, and 200 yuan from her husband, along with her own gold bracelets and watches, which she used to buy things. Now her husband wants her to go home, and as long as he doesn't hit her in the future, she is willing to go back, etc. Judge Ge verified the confessions and ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody, with the trial rescheduled for August 15. The stolen goods were first returned to the plaintiff.

Zhang Huanzhong

Suicide Due to Economic Pressure 117

Zhang Huanzhong, a 27-year-old from Ningbo, recently became unemployed and borrowed a room from his friend Zheng Hengda, also from Ningbo, at No. 22 Yuqingli, Xixinqiao, French Concession. He also entrusted Zheng and friends to find business opportunities. Feeling economically distressed, he suddenly had a suicidal thought. Around 5 PM the day before yesterday, he committed suicide by swallowing raw opium at Zheng's place. Zheng and others discovered this and rushed him to Renji Hospital. However, the opium poisoning had spread deeply, and he died around 7 PM that night despite treatment. The hospital notified the police, who sent detectives to move the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall autopsy station. Because no family members were found, the police reported to the Second District Court yesterday morning and commissioned Prosecutor Lou Guangguang, Clerk Zhao Yifen, and forensic doctor Wei Ligong to arrive at the station at 10 AM to examine the body. They confirmed that the body was that of Zhang Huanzhong. According to the Bao Detective, he had learned the previous situation. Zheng Hengda, a friend of the deceased, also testified that he and the deceased were friends, and that he committed suicide by taking poison due to unemployment and financial difficulties. After the discovery, his friends Wang Shigui and Ye Qingsheng accompanied him to the hospital for treatment. He has a mother who lives in Shanghai and works in a sock factory, but he does not know her address. He has already entrusted someone to find her, etc. The officials ruled that Zhang Huanzhong had committed suicide by taking poison. The body was temporarily collected by Tongren Fuyuan Hall, and Zheng Hengda was instructed to investigate his mother's address and bring her to identify the body. After the autopsy, the police took photos and the body was collected by the hall.

Continued Hearing on Zhu Shisheng's Sudden Death Case 118

Zhu's Two Daughters Unrelated

Lawsuit Withdrawn First

Zhu Shisheng, a local man who owned the Nanyang Department Store at No. 100 Yangshou Road, argued and wrestled with his step-wife, Zhu Zhang-shi, around 6 PM on the 24th of last month, and Zhu suddenly died. Zhang Xinglin, the son-in-law of Zhu's ex-wife, and daughters Zhang Zhu-shi and Zhu Zhu-shi, reported this to the police, who detained Zhu Zhang-shi and sent her to the Special District Court. Dr. Qin Daoyuan of Tongde Hospital determined that Zhu Shisheng had indeed died from a ruptured blood vessel. Both parties held their own views. After deliberation, a date was set for sentencing. The other day, Zhu Zhang-shi hired lawyers Lin Yingqing and Ye Fukan to sue Zhang Xinglin, Zhang Zhu-shi, and Zhu Zhu-shi for harming their parent. Judge Wu Tingqi opened the court for hearing. According to Zhu Zhang-shi, the reason for the dispute was that Zhang Xinglin had defrauded her of two receipts worth 40,000 taels of silver in the second month of the previous year, intending to embezzle them. She repeatedly demanded their return. On the evening of the 24th of last month, Zhang seized the opportunity and brought more than ten people to beat her and injure her. She had a medical certificate stored in the Yangshupu Police Station. Her husband, Zhu Shisheng, tried to mediate and was pushed and fell, resulting in fatal injuries. It was heard that one of the receipts had already been sold, and the other was kept at a certain lawyer's office. In reality, he had long planned to plot Zhu's family property. The witnesses he invited, Yuan Abao, Li Chunrong, and Yao Fuqing, were all bribed to falsely accuse her. When questioned, Zhang Xinglin and others did not admit to it. Judge Wu instructed Zhu Zhang-shi to re-examine her injuries. Zhang Zhu-shi and Zhu Zhu-shi were deemed unrelated, and the lawsuit was withdrawn first. The hearing was rescheduled for the witnesses to be brought to court for questioning.

The Publishing Industry Union was established yesterday

Branch Office of the World Bookstore 120

Immediately Proposed Thirteen Treatment Conditions

The World Bookstore Branch Office of the Municipal Publishing Industry Union held a membership meeting at 8 AM yesterday at the World Bookstore Main Factory on Dalianwan Road, formally establishing itself. The Publishing Industry Union notified the bureau in advance, requesting a three-hour suspension of work to allow members to participate. The bureau itself announced a day off. On that day, more than 500 people attended, including representatives Wu Jiaze from the Municipal Party Department, Gu Bingyuan from the Social Bureau, Wang Wenhua from the Publishing Industry Union, Chen Yuesheng from the Commercial Branch Office, Huang Zhuting from the China Branch Office, and all employees. Yang Youren, the newly appointed representative to the 15th International Labour Conference, also attended the meeting. The election results and a summary of the conditions are recorded separately below.

Election of Directors The public elected Ni Guangming, Zhang Sigen, Zhang Wenbin, Zhai Gusun, and Hong Zhonghua as the presidium. After the ceremonial proceedings, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting. Representatives of the Party and government agencies delivered training speeches (the speeches are omitted). Ni Guangming, Zhang Sigen, Zhang Wenbin, Gu Xinggen, Xu Zhijie, Su Yixia, Hong Zhonghua, Zhai Gusun, Chen Ningting, and other nine people were elected as directors. Li Dixing, Xi Lindu, Zhang Juntao, and Xi Yuanshen were elected as alternate directors. They were sworn into office on the spot.

Summary of Conditions After the World Bookstore's employees established a branch office, they immediately prepared to request improved treatment from the capitalists. Thirteen conditions were proposed and approved by the conference. The summary is as follows. First, the company should recognize the right of the Shanghai Publishing Industry Union to represent the members of the World Bookstore Branch Office and must subsidize the branch office's operating expenses by 400 yuan per month. Second, salary increases: A. The current minimum wage standard is 25 yuan. Those whose original wage is below 25 yuan will receive an additional 10 yuan (if the increase still does not bring them to 25 yuan, it must be brought up to 25 yuan). Those from 26 to 30 yuan will receive an additional 9 yuan, those from 31 to 35 yuan will receive an additional 8 yuan, those from 36 to 40 yuan will receive an additional 6 yuan, and those above 41 yuan will receive an additional 5 yuan. This applies equally to male and female workers. B. Annual salary increases should be based on the overall average monthly salary of all employees of the Shanghai Head Office, according to the increase in the cost of living, as the standard for universally increasing everyone's salary. If there are odd numbers less than an integer, they should be rounded up to the nearest yuan. For example, if the overall average monthly salary of all employees in the company is 30 yuan and the cost of living index for the 19th year is assumed to be 100 points, and it increases to 110 points for the 20th year, then from January of the 20th year, each person should receive a universal salary increase of 3 yuan per month. The rest is analogous. Both items A and B of the salary increase are proportionate for pieceworkers and contractors. Fourth, working hours: the printing factory and distribution office should have a maximum of eight hours per day. Overtime on weekdays and overtime at night should be calculated at half a day's work for every two hours and one day's work for every four hours. The maximum overtime per day should not exceed four hours, and the maximum overtime per week should not exceed four days. Ninth, workers will uniformly get three days of sick leave per month. Pieceworkers and contractors will be paid proportionately. Eleventh, double pay will be issued at the end of the year. Pieceworkers and contractors will be handled uniformly. Thirteenth, when the company closes its accounts each year, one-tenth of the total surplus will be taken for public debt funds, then 5% for dividends, and the remaining five-tenths will be used for worker bonuses and five-tenths for shareholder dividends.

Flooding in Various Districts of the City 123

The Social Bureau Sent Personnel to Investigate

Last month, there were continuous heavy rains, the river tide rose sharply, and the river water suddenly increased, resulting in standing water in low-lying areas. Cotton, rice, melons, and beans were mostly submerged. In addition, the weather was changeable, suddenly cold and hot, which had a significant impact on the growth of crops. For example, in Pudong, where the terrain is relatively high and the drainage is good, the cotton and beans were in the flowering and fruiting stage, the rice was sprouting, and the melons were being harvested. After this continuous rain and cold, the roots rotted, the leaves withered, and growth stopped, which is very regrettable. After the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau received reports from municipal councilors in the Fahua and other districts about the flooding, it sent personnel to various districts to investigate. This has now been completed. The inspection report will be compiled, and statistics will be submitted to the government for the record, and plans will be made to provide relief.

Red Cross Society The Chinese Red Cross Society received a telegram from member Feng Liangfei stating that on the fifth day of the sixth lunar month, there was heavy rain, which continued until the tenth day. Torrential floods, originating from Huizhou, Shexian, Jingxian, and Jingxian, flowed straight down, bursting the river in Dongmei Village, Xixiang, Xuanyi County, and changing the river course. The waters of the Tongjin Bridge and the Qiyi and Hanting Rivers converged at Xixihe Town, washing away seventy or eighty shops, as well as the Tao family in Taojiayuan. A total of more than 1,000 people were drowned. It was even more tragic than the Yijiang flood of the eleventh year. Except for the Luo Gong and Shen Gong embankments, the Taifeng and other embankments in Nanyi, the downstream area, were breached, and corpses were floating everywhere, beyond rescue. The smoke from cooking fires was almost extinguished for hundreds of miles, and epidemics were rampant, with no food or medicine available, leading to imminent death. These are all confirmed circumstances. Liangfei, as a member, could not bear to stand idly by. He attached a film showing the tragic situation and sent a telegram to the president and chairman of the board, requesting an urgent relief effort to relieve the pressing needs. Both the living and the dead will be grateful. Member Feng Liangfei sends his heartfelt greetings. The Chinese Nationalist Party's Dangtu County Party Affairs Rectification Committee in Anhui Province telegraphed the Chinese Red Cross Society stating that Dangtu borders rivers and lakes, and the land is mostly low-lying. Heavy rain fell in the summer, causing floods. The areas where the floods spread have destroyed 500,000 to 600,000 mu of fields and affected no fewer than 200,000 people. On nights of bitter rain and chilling winds, the sound of heartbroken cries is often heard. In the midst of terrifying waves, countless white bones are swept away. Homes are destroyed, villages are reduced to ruins, belongings are gone, and crops are lost. The situation is truly unprecedented in recent decades. The Daguan embankment, which is related to the economic lifeline of the county's rural areas, was also breached by the rising river tide. Observing the gaunt faces and the hunger on the roads, with no wheat or rice, how can the common people be consoled? Our association feels ashamed for lacking the ability to turn stones into gold, making it difficult to preserve the remaining people. We can only call out on behalf of the suffering and hope to alleviate the disaster in the night. We have always admired your reputation for righteousness and your enthusiasm for saving the people. We dare to ask you to quickly distribute relief grain so that the disaster victims can receive the grace of your benevolence, be reborn with joy, and alleviate the great suffering of the drought fish. The benefits will be limitless. In urgent circumstances, we cannot choose our words carefully. Please examine this carefully. The Chinese Nationalist Party's Dangtu County Party Affairs in Anhui reverently implores.

Since the beginning of the month, there has been continuous heavy rain, and the embankments and fields on the southwest and east sides have collapsed and been completely submerged. The livestock, houses, and rations have also been washed away. All 360,000 people in the county have been affected. Cooking fires have been extinguished, and there is no sound of chickens or dogs. The situation is extremely critical and cannot be sustained. The Jiangsu Xiaoxian County Government telegraphed that since May, there has been heavy rain, the worst in more than a decade. The entire county has become a swamp, and boats can be rowed on flat ground. The autumn crops have been completely submerged, and countless houses have collapsed. The source of livelihood has been cut off, and there is extreme panic. The Jiangsu Baoying people telegraphed that there has been a lot of rain this summer, and the rivers and lakes have risen. The embankments have collapsed one after another, and countless houses and fields have been washed away. Hundreds of miles are covered in water. Residents have nowhere to live, clinging to the tops of trees, swaying in the wind and rain, and calling for help with no way to get it. It is unbearable to see people waiting to die. The Jiangsu Huai'an Public Law Groups telegraphed that the county has suffered disasters for the past three years, and the people have been unable to bear it. Unexpectedly, there has been continuous heavy rain since July. The embankments and fields in the four rural areas have been submerged one after another, and many fields and houses have been washed away. Tens of thousands of victims are crying to the heavens. The Fuyang and Yingzhou Water Disaster Relief Temporary Committee sent a public letter stating that since the harvest of two wheat crops in mid-June of this year, there has been continuous rain for a month. Then, mountain floods broke out, and Jiaoshui flooded across the countryside. In an instant, thousands of miles turned into swamps. In low-lying areas, people could not escape and were buried in the stomachs of fish with their families. Countless livestock and houses were washed away, leaving nothing behind. Those who were fortunate enough to escape were displaced, with only their lives spared. Family members were lost, and they had no food or clothing. They cried out for hunger and help. The situation was too terrible to bear, and relief was urgently needed.

High Water on the Yangtze River Impedes Shipping 125

Chongqing Cannot Unload Goods This time the high water disaster, from the lower reaches of the Yangtze River, reached all the way to the Sichuan River, covering the provinces of Jiangsu, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, and Sichuan. Shipping on the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River has been hindered. Chongqing, Sichuan, was initially still open for freight, but on the 7th, there was heavy rain again, and the river water in Chongqing suddenly rose, 24 feet higher than usual. It has already flooded the shore. The local shipping companies received a telegram from that port yesterday saying that the streets have been submerged in water, and goods cannot be loaded or unloaded at the docks. Ships arriving in Chongqing cannot unload their cargo, and cargo going downstream has no way to board ships. Transportation on the Sichuan River will be interrupted.

Hankou Barges Enter the City Efforts are being made to pump out the floodwaters in Hankou, but there was heavy rain again the day before yesterday, causing the floodwaters in the city to deepen. The cargo warehouses on the docks of the various ships that had not built dikes were completely submerged in water. Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, and China Merchants warehouses, which took earlier precautions, also had water depths of about a foot in the lower levels. According to Hankou's telegram yesterday, the passengers and cargo of the various river ships that arrived in Hankou on the 7th were transferred by small barges directly into the city. The streets and roads were purely used for boat crossings to provide transportation to and from the city. Many of the goods going from Shanghai were stopped from loading unless they were urgently needed. The goods that were being rushed were the necessities of life, such as white rice, wheat flour, sugar, piece goods, cotton yarn, and medicine. The rest of the goods have been temporarily stopped from loading.

Chen Yongxing's Fishing Boat Was Sunk by a Small Steamer 128

The Crew Was Safe

Chen Yongxing, a fishing boat from Ningbo, loaded with sand and jellyfish from Sijiao Mountain, came to Shanghai to sell its goods. On the evening of the day before yesterday (the 7th), when it was sailing to the surface of the Shahua kerosene pool in Gaohua, Songnan, it happened to encounter a small steamer of a certain company towing a barge. Education News

Important News 137

Hunan Provincial Government 138

Subsidies for Educational Institutions Affected by Disasters 139

Changsha Dispatch: Among the areas harmed by the Communists, Hunan is second only to Jiangxi in the severity of the damage. In the past two years, approximately thirty counties in Hunan Province have been raided by Communist bandits. The losses of public and private property are incalculable. In terms of educational institutions, many local libraries and popular education centers have been burned down. As for schools, they have either been burned or destroyed. As a result, they are unable to open, or if they do open, they face many difficulties due to inadequate equipment, which greatly hinders the progress of education. Therefore, He Jian has allocated 60,000 yuan from disaster relief funds to the Department of Education to be distributed based on the severity of the damage. Huang Zhengheng convened a joint meeting of the heads of relevant institutions at 2:00 PM on the 3rd, attended by over ten people. Hu Yiru presided over the meeting. After formal greetings, the following items were discussed:

(1) How should the funds be distributed between the provincial capital and the counties affected by the Communist bandits? It was decided that 60% (36,000 yuan) would be distributed to the counties and 40% (24,000 yuan) to the provincial capital.

(2) From what time period should the educational institutions affected by the Communist bandits be considered? It was decided to include institutions affected from July 1920 to July 18, 1921.

(3) How should the counties affected by the Communist bandits be classified for subsidies? It was decided to divide the counties into two categories, A and B, except for Pingjiang and Liuyang counties, which have already been approved for subsidies by the provincial government and will not be included in this allocation. (A) Counties that have been captured by Communist bandits two or more times will be classified as Category A, including six counties: Huarong, Chaling, Nanxian, Youxian, Anren, and Poyang, each receiving 1,800 yuan. (B) Counties that have been captured by Communist bandits once, or have not been captured but have suffered severe damage from banditry, will be classified as Category B, including seventeen counties: Changsha, Yueyang, Xiangyin, Shimen, Linli, Lixian, Liling, Sangzhi, Zixing, Yongxing, Tongdao, Anxiang, Daoxian, Cili, Dayong, Wugang, and Xinning, each receiving 1,000 yuan. (3) The remaining 3,200 yuan will be kept in the custody of the Department of Education to be used as needed. It was decided to pass the motion.

(4) Should provincial educational institutions that have suffered losses from Communist bandits be subsidized? It was decided that, except for the Library and Museum, which have not yet been restored, provincial educational institutions that have already been restored will not be subsidized.

(5) On what basis should the educational institutions in the provincial capital that have suffered losses from bandits be subsidized? It was decided that: (A) The Library and Museum will each receive 5,000 yuan, totaling 10,000 yuan, as a foundation for restoration. (B) Subsidies will be divided into five categories: A, B, C, D, and E, based on reported losses. Losses of 20,000 yuan or more will be classified as Category A, 10,000 yuan or more as Category B, 5,000 yuan or more as Category C, 2,000 yuan or more as Category D, and less than 2,000 yuan as Category E. (C) Each school in Category A will receive 900 yuan, Category B 500 yuan, Category C 350 yuan, Category D 250 yuan, and Category E 150 yuan. (D) The remaining funds will be kept in the custody of the Department of Education to be used as needed.

(6) How should the use of the subsidies be regulated? It was decided that they should be used exclusively for educational equipment and not for personal losses. Furthermore, the Department of Education should be notified of the equipment purchased for record keeping. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Ministry of Education

Instructions Regarding Teaching Methods 141

Order to the Department of Education of the Eastern Provinces Special District

The Ministry of Education, according to the Department of Education of the Eastern Provinces Special District, submitted an inspection report for the first semester of the 19th year for review. The Ministry of Education instructed that the report and the submitted documents are noted. It is found that the criticisms of the conditions of elementary and middle schools in various subjects by the inspectors are quite detailed, and the Department's rewards and punishments are handled appropriately. However, upon reviewing the report, it appears that the teaching methods in various elementary and middle schools completely adopt the lecture method. There is too little spontaneous activity by students in the classroom, which is inappropriate. The Department should instruct all schools to study the teaching methods of each subject in the future, appropriately reduce lecture-style teaching based on the nature of the curriculum, and guide students to learn independently in order to improve teaching effectiveness. This should be followed accordingly.

Zhejiang Province's Education Expenses in Arrears in Various Counties

Educational Bonds Issued to Repay Loans 142

Educational funding in various counties of Zhejiang Province is stretched thin, and all feel financially exhausted. Therefore, during months of peak land tax collection, the surcharge income can barely provide support. However, during off-peak collection periods, it is necessary to borrow money to cope. Now that county treasuries have been established and provincial and local taxes have been separated, there is no room for diversion of funds. If loans are taken from private banks, the interest rates are very high during normal times, and even higher during times of financial stringency, requiring discount losses. The annual interest rate is estimated to be around 2%. If the principal cannot be repaid when due, the interest is compounded, further increasing the burden. If this continues, the educational funding of various counties may eventually become bankrupt. It is now proposed that various counties issue educational bonds specifically to repay educational loans and not to be used for other purposes. These bonds can be easily raised locally. The annual interest rate will be half that of loans from private banks, and the reduced interest can be saved for future repayment of the principal. This seems to be a win-win situation. This proposal was previously resolved by the Education Bureau of this province for educational funding, and can be used by the counties with deficits as a reference. The Department of Education has now approved the measures, and the counties will consider their current situations and decide whether to issue bonds. The measures are recorded below:

1. When issuing these bonds, each county must first submit a report to the provincial government for approval and record keeping.

2. The total amount of bonds issued by each county shall be no less than 5,000 yuan and no more than 20,000 yuan.

3. The annual interest rate of these bonds shall be 7%.

4. At a rate of ____% public____, the actual revenue will be 98%.

5. Within five years, interest shall be paid in two installments per year. After five years, 20% of the principal shall be repaid each year by drawing lots.

6. These bonds shall be guaranteed by the educational surcharge revenue of each county, and a certain amount of national currency shall be set aside each year from the surcharge and deposited in a reputable bank, with half used for interest payments and half used for principal repayments after five years.

7. The bond interest coupons may be used to offset educational surcharges on land tax and ____ funds.

Jiangyin Education Budget Inadequate 143

The educational budget for the 20th year in Jiangyin, after being repeatedly revised by the Education Bureau and submitted to the county government for forwarding to the Department of Education, has been instructed to the effect that the submitted budget did not comply with the previous order to modify the number of mu donations for the Yishe (righteous society) and due to actual deficits, they dare not use them and therefore they were not included. The method is actually inappropriate. Even if they intend to protect customers, the actual shortage of donations to Yishe, should also be included in the second reserve fund and indicating the number of months. It should be returned for rewriting. The educational plan is generally appropriate, but attention should be paid to several points: (1) The one-year rural normal undergraduate program should be temporarily suspended and the funds used for equipment. (2) The title of substitute elementary school should be canceled and changed to district-run, but standards should be set. (3) The compulsory practice area should be changed to a compulsory education test area, and a preliminary plan for elementary school should be quickly drafted and submitted for approval before it can be opened. (4) New schools or grades must be submitted for approval before they can be started or funds can be spent. (5) The establishment and implementation of the Civil Education Center must be carried out in accordance with the Department's Order No. 6058.

Free Talk

A Word of Insight 163

— Qiu Shui

Language should not be rude or violent, as that is not gentlemanly. However, it should also not be overly restrained, as that is not elegant.

A saying goes, "Words are the voice of the heart." However, are there not those in the world who speak insincerely? How is this saying to be interpreted then?

The true essence of freedom is responsibility. Therefore, those who truly understand freedom will never demand it.

If people could all understand the true meaning of truth, money, and success, then they would naturally treat others with frankness, generosity, and humility.

A person's intelligence or foolishness is not determined by the amount of their experience, but by the extent of their ability to acquire experience.

Those who stare at women's faces on the street like eagles swooping down on chickens are not necessarily lustful. The mere act of "looking" is not enough to satisfy the desires of a "lustful" person.

To elevate the character of women, the first thing to do is to abolish bizarre and glamorous clothing. Bizarre and glamorous clothing can only gain the love of men, but is not enough to gain admiration. The more one seeks love from others, the more base one's character becomes.

Killing a foreigner in China can lead to China's immediate demise. Killing thousands of Chinese people abroad results in nothing being said or done. There is no justice or humanity in the world. If there is, it only comes from the mouths of the weak.

Boycotting Japanese goods is not because the Chinese people's enthusiasm is low and can only last for five minutes, but because there are many things that we must rely on them for. Therefore, to permanently boycott Japanese goods, the best thing to do is to promote domestic products.

Colonel Lindbergh's Flight to China 164

— Lü Bing

Colonel Lindbergh's recent long-distance flight passed through the Far East. Our country will prepare an international reception to express our welcome. People in Shanghai, hearing this news, all consider it fortunate to have a glimpse of the world's most famous aviator. The success of Lindbergh's flight was truly in May 1927. At that time, Lindbergh created an unprecedented record for the air route between Paris and New York. For a time, his name spread far and wide, and newspapers in various countries published as much information as possible about his achievements and photos. People in France and America, in particular, were wildly enthusiastic throughout the country. Wherever Lindbergh set foot, unplanned gatherings often resulted in streets being deserted.

Regarding Lindbergh's past, one thing he can be proud of is that in the three months after his successful flight between America and France, the number of letters and telegrams he received was the highest in the world. According to statistics at the time, in less than sixty days, he received more than three and a half million congratulatory letters, more than ten thousand congratulatory telegrams, and approximately 15,000 parcels of gifts. Postal and telegraph personnel in Europe and America specially worked overtime for Lindbergh, busy coping with the situation, which was a phenomenon that had never been seen before.

Lindbergh, having received such a flood of letters and telegrams, should have replied to them as a matter of course. Therefore, in 1927, when he was in Paris, he specifically rented a huge residence for the purpose of handling personal replies. The American Minister, Mr. Herrick, specially sent eight secretaries to assist him in his work. Unexpectedly, the letters were like snowflakes, almost causing the eight secretaries to be dumbfounded and unable to handle them. Later, he borrowed fifteen secretaries from the Paris Chamber of Commerce before he was able to send out more than 200,000 reply letters and thank-you notes in six weeks.

The above sections are all recorded in European and American newspapers and magazines, and are not conjecture. Recollecting Lindbergh's sensation throughout the global community was like this. It can truly be said that he is the most famous person in the aviation world of this century. I am bringing this up before Lindbergh flies through the Far East, hoping that it will also be something that readers will be happy to know about.

Wuxi's White Little Maiden Melon 165

— Meng Die

The melons of Wuxi, there is one named White Little Maiden, which is a fine variety. It is produced in places such as Shitangwan and Luoshe. It is small and oval in shape, a type of sweet melon. Its color is pure white like jade, crystal clear like snow. Its fragrance spreads far and wide, like that of a snow pear. Its taste is sweet and tender, hence the name. It is just like the lychee being called Green-Clad Lad, or the pine tree being named Grey-Bearded Elder, and this is even more beautiful. A friend bought some yesterday as a gift, and included a note saying, "To dispel heat and generate coolness, I present the White Little Maiden. No need for a golden house, please taste this special flavor. If you deem it a precious gift, please compose a new poem." I received it and played with it, then ate it, feeling that its appearance was pleasing and its taste even more so. Surely a poem is needed. Therefore, I casually composed a poem to praise it, saying, "Moon-like beauty, snow-like skin, emerging from the fields with graceful form. Why compare your jade body to Sweet Gan? You should be called Fen'er instead. Stealing coolness and dispelling the summer heat, quenching thirst and comforting longing. Pity that you are marrying a man of money, like a cardamom bud about to bloom." This is also a poem on objects with a unique flavor.

An Account of Zhu Yongkui's Exquisite Ivory Carving Skills 166

— Yan Chonglou

Zhu Yongkui from Kuimen has exquisite ivory carving skills. He can carve hundreds of characters on a piece of ivory the size of a melon seed, in various scripts. Through a friend's introduction, I got to know him. Zhu is just over twenty years old. He studies in Shanghai, is intelligent and eager to learn, but is taciturn. Those who do not know him are unaware that he possesses such skills.

I work at the Wuzhou Pharmacy. One day, Zhu came to visit, bringing with him an ivory seal he had carved. The seal was less than an inch long and not even a third of an inch wide. Yet on one side, he had carved the entire "Spring Rhapsody" by Yu Xin, totaling more than four hundred characters. The naked eye could barely make them out. But when viewed under a microscope, the characters were slender and firm, and the rows were neat and orderly. Everyone present passed it around, marveling at it. A colleague asked, "Ancient people praised excellent carvings as being done by the hands of ghosts. Your skill surpasses that of the ancients. Is there some secret technique involved?" Zhu replied, "These are all exaggerations. When I was seven or eight years old, I enjoyed carving. At first, I only carved larger things. Then, I gradually moved from large to small, from small to tiny. After more than ten years of practice, I can now use the tools freely. Skill comes from practice. There is no other way." Zhu's words were like this. I, however, believe that the achievement of an art is half due to human effort and half due to natural talent. Zhu is perhaps too modest in his words. However, this further demonstrates his virtue of not boasting about his talents.

Tragic News of the Flood in Furong Embankment 167

— Ren Nongxuan

About fifty li outside the North Gate of Wuxi, there is a large embankment called Furong. It was originally Furong Lake. Every autumn, many hibiscus flowers were produced, hence the name. During the Ming dynasty, Zhou Wenxiang, Minister of Works, came here on a southern inspection tour. He used soldiers instead of laborers to manage the lake and turn it into fields. Since then, farmers from various places have come to cultivate the land, and it has been more than four hundred years. It is sixty-three square li in circumference, with a total of 68,000 mu of fields and more than 200,000 farmers. It borders Jiangyin and Wujin counties. The terrain is low-lying, shaped like an upturned cauldron. It is known as land unsuitable for wheat. It is surrounded by mountains on all sides, where the virtuous Lu Guimeng of old lived in seclusion. Unexpectedly, at the end of June this summer, continuous rain fell. The water in the fields accumulated to about three feet. Most farmers rented water pumps to try to save the crops. At a time when silkworms were devastated, economic difficulties were severe. They pawned their clothes and bedding, hoping to save the rotting seedlings and salvage something. However, after everything had been pawned and they could borrow no more, on the afternoon of July 18, dark clouds suddenly gathered again, and torrential rain poured down, accompanied by mountain torrents. The river water outside the embankment rose sharply by more than ten feet. In about a week, a total of four feet and eight inches of rain fell. The fields and gardens turned into a watery kingdom, boundless and without end. This year's autumn harvest is completely hopeless. It is now reported that all the farmers, big and small, in the embankment are living in waterlogged houses, sleeping on planks. Kitchens have become canals, and they are cooking with urns, exposed to the wind and dew, crying out for food. The various tragic scenes are unbearable to witness. Therefore, the township head and others have jointly submitted a report to the county government, requesting immediate relief. We deeply hope that philanthropists within the country will generously donate to help these disaster victims. (No payment accepted)

Reminiscences of Spending Summer at West Lake (II) 168

— Yuan Rongfang

In recent years, the lotus flowers on the lake, those at Three Pools Mirroring the Moon, are the best. Every May and June when the flowers bloom, tourists flock there. It is as Yuan Mei said, "Amidst the deep red lotus flowers, painted boats are added." The pools are in the middle of the lake, and one must take a gondola to get there. It is hotter at noon. I went there either early in the morning or late in the evening. The houses there are winding, and the flowers and trees are lush. The character pavilion is built in the water, connected on all sides by winding stone bridges. The vermilion railings are hidden, as if entering a painting. It is a great place to admire the lotus flowers. Leaning on the railing and looking around, one sees round canopies swaying with greenery, long hairpins blooming with red. The clear fragrance is intoxicating, like drinking fine wine. An ancient poem says, "Enjoying the world of white lotus flowers, lying in the middle with the wind coming from all directions." This can be experienced here.

Lingyin Temple has secluded scenery, and its coolness is especially suitable for summer. Since the construction of the Circum-Lake Road, motorcycles can go directly to outside the Huilong Bridge. One can go in the morning and return in the evening, making transportation convenient. Therefore, more and more people visit. Every summer, wearing a linen shirt and holding a banana leaf fan, I often wander under Feilai Peak. Feilai Peak is located in front of Yunlin Temple. The jade screen stands tall, strangely protruding and winding, possessing the wonders of thinness, transparency, and wrinkling. Ancient trees and strange trees grow all around the peak. Iron trunks and withered branches have roots growing in stone gullies. Emerald umbrellas are layered, forming an emerald canopy. One sees only green clouds filling the sky and emerald shade covering the ground. Sometimes, the wind blows, moving the trees, and fragmented sunlight leaks through the gaps in the trees, flickering and swaying on the rocks, as if spying on people. It is especially interesting to appreciate the flying spring in the Cold Spring Pavilion or the Helai Pavilion. Splashing white and dripping emerald, winding and zigzagging, tinkling like playing the zither and zither. The wind rustles through the stone gullies, and the coolness penetrates the bones. The mind and spirit are refreshed, giving one a feeling of wanting to become an immortal. Every time I go to Lingyin, I linger, reluctant to leave.

Yunqi is located in the northwest of Wuyun Mountain. I love Lingyin for its openness, and I love Yunqi for its seclusion. It is a pity that it is farther from the city. From the city, take a motorcycle to Liuhe Pagoda, pass Fancun, and go north for several li to Sanju Pavilion. Then, walk another hundred steps to Xixin Pavilion. The entire way is a winding path, paved with stones in a shattered ice pattern. The moss is thick in the cracks of the stones. Walking on it is like walking on brocade. Tens of thousands of tall bamboos surround the path, blocking the sun. One only feels the greenness assaulting the eyes and the coolness assailing the sleeves. The seclusion and beauty are indescribable. Every time I walk in it, I walk slowly, fearing that the beautiful scenery will soon end. The chirping of birds is pleasant to the ear, like playing immortal music. Xixin Pavilion faces north, with two windows opening, reflecting the green smoke. The sound of the spring is ding-dong, like the tinkling of jade pendants. Resting for a while, the dust is washed away, and coolness arises from the elbows and armpits, almost forgetting that it is high summer. Going further, one is surrounded by ancient trees. Yunlin Temple is there.

Fiction Relief Association

Woman, Woman (14) 169

— Yao Su Feng

Like a newly married couple going on their honeymoon, everything feels warm and sweet. They can forget the shaking of the wheels, forget the fatigue of the journey, as if in a fleeting moment, they have arrived in Suzhou.

Still the sound of cars, the sound of people, jumping around the station, Mr. Lu did not feel any different from two days ago, but Miss Ding was harboring endless new interest. The car stopped, she poked her head out of the car window to look at the scenery at the station.

"Ayao...gardenia...flower?..." From the chaos of shouts, she suddenly grasped a lovely soft Wu dialect; then there was a thick, greasy floral fragrance lingering in her nostrils.

"Buy flowers!" she shouted.

Mr. Lu was carrying his suitcase, preparing to get off the bus. When he heard Miss Ding shouting to buy flowers, his heart jumped. But when he glanced out the car window and saw a woman carrying a basket of flowers running towards him quickly, he felt the urgency of the moment even more.

He had no choice but to deliberately turn his back to the car window, take out two dimes from his pocket, hurriedly throw them on the small table, look at the other side, and his heart kept pounding wildly.

Miss Ding insisted on pulling him and asking, "Do you want to sell two flowers too?"

"Alright! Let's get off the bus! The bus is leaving soon!" He was extremely embarrassed.

The flower-selling woman outside the car window did not initially notice who was standing in the car window after the first transaction was successful. But when Miss Ding turned her head and asked Mr. Lu, she could not help but look up, expecting a second transaction. It was then that she became suspicious.

She only felt that the man's back looked just like her family's Xiao Rong, but she could not be sure whether the man was indeed Xiao Rong or not. She stared intently, but the man never turned around. Finally, she laughed at herself. She just thought; the man and the woman came together: if it was really Xiao Rong, how could he be with such a beautiful woman? So she laughed at her own suspicion and went to find other customers with her basket.

On the other side, Mr. Lu hurriedly pulled Miss Ding off the bus, trying hard to avoid being discovered by his wife: with great difficulty, he squeezed out of the station in the crowd, and only then did he feel relieved.

Unexpectedly, another sharp shout made Mr. Lu unable to help but secretly cry out in pain.

"Xiao Rong! Xiao Rong!" Mr. Lu could clearly hear that it was the voice of the young boy on his family's carriage.

At first, he wanted to pretend he didn't hear, but the young boy was already standing beside him.
